Adopting Another Madhhab for Oppressed Women: Conditions and Limits
Explanation of permissibility to adopt Maliki school for cases not solved in Hanafi fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a Hanafi mufti may adopt a fatwa from another madhhab (such as Maliki) and apply them to a case of extreme necessity.

Core Idea
A Hanafi mufti may adopt another madhhab only under extreme necessity, with conditions, and without violating Hanafi usul.

This lesson explores a crucial tool in the mufti's arsenal: the permissible adoption of another madhhab when the Hanafi school offers no remedy for a genuine hardship. The author, Maulana Ashraf Ali Thanwi, illustrates this by presenting fatwas obtained from Maliki muftis for oppressed women. Understanding the precise conditions—extreme necessity, consultation, and full adherence to the adopted madhhab—is essential for proper ifta.

Guided Path
1
Identify the unresolved case in Hanafi fiqh
Recognize that the problem at hand (e.g., a woman seeking tafriq) has no clear solution within the Hanafi school. The passage notes a 'shortage' of such cases in Hanafi fiqh.
This step requires thorough knowledge of Hanafi rulings to confirm the gap.
2
Assess the level of necessity (darurah)
Determine whether the situation reaches the level of extreme hardship (shiddat darurah) that warrants leaving the default school. The passage emphasizes 'extreme necessity' as the trigger.
Not every difficulty justifies departure; it must be genuinely unbearable.
3
Consult qualified scholars of the other madhhab
The author obtained fatwas from Maliki muftis in Madinah. This demonstrates that the mufti must rely on specialists of that school, not on his own incomplete knowledge.
Correspondence with experts ensures the fatwa is authentic within that madhhab.
4
Apply the conditions and restrictions (shara'it wa quyudat)
The adoption is not absolute. The mufti must follow the other madhhab in all its requirements for that specific case and avoid talfiq (mixing rulings in a way that violates principles).
The passage explicitly states 'مع شرائط و قیودات' (with conditions and restrictions).
5
Issue the fatwa ensuring no contradiction with Hanafi usul
Before issuing, verify that the adopted ruling does not conflict with a definitive (qat'i) Hanafi principle. The fatwa should be presented as an exceptional concession for this particular necessity.
The objection that 'Islam has no such solution' is refuted by the existence of this valid Sharia remedy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسرے مذہب پر فتوی دینے کی حد بعض شرائط مذکورہ جواب اگر چہ اعتراض کرنے والوں کے لیے کافی ہے لیکن اس جگہ ایک اشکال یہ باقی رہ جاتا ہے کہ شوہر کے طلاق دیتے بغیر یا شوہر کی وفات کے بغیر بھی تفریق شرعی یعنی علیحدگی کی کوئی صورت ہے یا نہیں ؟ اگر چہ مذکورہ جواب کے بعد مزید جواب کی ضرورت باقی نہیں رہ جاتی لیکن کیونکہ اس جواب میں مظلوم عورتوں کی مشکلات کا شرعی حل ہے اس وجہ سے ہم تبر گا اس جواب کو بھی پیش کرتے ہیں ۔
مظلوم عورتوں کیلئے گنجائش جن عورتوں کا ابھی نکاح نہیں ہوا ان کی قسم قسم کی تکالیف دور کرنے کے لیے فقہ حنفی میں ایسے مسائل کی کمی ہے اس وجہ سے اس طرح کے واقعات کے متعلق مدینہ منورہ سے چند مرتبہ خط و کتابت کے بعد مذہب مالکیہ کے مفتیان کرام سے منادی حاصل کیے گئے یہ فتاوی جو کہ مع سوال و جواب عربی میں ہیں اس کتاب کے دوسرے جنود العنوان مجموعہ فتاولی مالکیہ میں مذکور ہیں) اس جواب کے بعد اور شدید ضرورت میں دوسرے امام کے مسلک کو مع شرائط و قیودات اختیار کر لینے کی گنجائش کے بعد اس اعتراض کی گنجائش نہیں کہ " اسلام میں کوئی ایسی تدبیر نہیں کہ جن میں قاضی شرط ہو"
The limit of giving fatwa according to another madhhab. The above answer with some conditions is sufficient for the objectors, but here one difficulty remains: is there any form of Sharia separation (i.e., dissolution of marriage) without the husband giving divorce or without the husband's death? Although after the above answer there is no further need for reply, but because in this answer there is a Sharia solution for the difficulties of oppressed women, therefore we voluntarily present this answer as well. Concession for oppressed women: To relieve various kinds of sufferings of women who have not yet been married [or: who are in difficult marriages], there is a lack of such cases in Hanafi fiqh. Therefore, regarding such incidents, after several correspondences with Madinah Munawwarah, rulings (fatwas) were obtained from the honorable muftis of the Maliki school. These fatwas, along with questions and answers in Arabic, are mentioned in the second section of this book, 'Majmu'ah Fatawa Maliki'. After this answer and after the permission to adopt the madhhab of another imam under extreme necessity with conditions and restrictions, there is no room for the objection that 'There is no such solution in Islam that requires a judge as a condition.'
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage addresses a remaining objection: whether a Sharia separation (khul' or tafriq) is possible without a divorce or death. The author explains that while the previous answer suffices, he presents an additional solution for oppressed women. He notes that Hanafi fiqh lacks sufficient solutions for some hardships faced by women. Therefore, after consulting with Maliki muftis in Madinah, they obtained fatwas from the Maliki school. These are compiled in a separate section. The key point is that under extreme necessity, it is permissible to adopt the ruling of another imam (here, Imam Malik) with specific conditions and restrictions. This removes any objection that Islam offers no solution unless a Sharia judge is present. The passage teaches that adopting another madhhab is a valid hila (legal stratagem) when the Hanafi school has no remedy and necessity demands it.

Key Terms
تفریق شرعی (tafrīq shar‘ī): Judicial separation or dissolution of marriage granted by a Sharia judge.
مذہب مالکیہ (madhhab Mālikiyyah): The Maliki school of Islamic law, one of the four Sunni schools.
حیلۂ شرعیہ (hīlah shar‘iyyah): A lawful stratagem or legal device to achieve a permissible end without violating Sharia.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author obtain fatwas from Maliki muftis?
A) Because Hanafis dislike their own school
B) Because Hanafi fiqh lacked sufficient solutions for oppressed women
C) Because the Maliki muftis were more accessible
D) Because the author personally follows the Maliki school

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti may adopt another madhhab only under extreme necessity, with conditions, and after consulting qualified scholars of that madhhab.

Consulting Lawyers for Shar'i Implementation of Hila Cases
Instruction to consult lawyers for legal compliance of hila cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a practical plan for implementing a hila shari'iyyah that includes consulting legal experts to ensure compliance with government law while preserving shar'i validity.

Core Idea
A hila is only effective when implemented within the bounds of both Sharia and state law.

This lesson addresses a critical practical step for muftis: how to implement a shar'i stratagem (hila) in a non-Islamic legal system. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, instructs a Shar'i committee to consult lawyers to ensure proceedings align with government law. This reflects the Hanafi principle that while shar'i rulings are supreme, their implementation may require compliance with secular law as a matter of necessity. We will parse this instruction and extract the operative guidance for a contemporary mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary directive
The passage instructs the Shar'i committee to consult lawyers. What specific aspect of the case is to be checked? The answer: whether the case proceedings are in accordance with or against government law.
2
Distinguish the roles
Clarify that the committee confirms shar'i validity, while lawyers verify legal compliance. They are distinct and complementary.
3
Recognize the motivation
The author mentions objectors against religion. This consultation is to avoid unnecessary conflict and to remove obstacles.
4
Apply to a modern scenario
Consider a hila for interest-based loans. Implementation requires both shar'i permissibility and government legal form.
5
Note the call for approval
The author urges influential persons to seek legal recognition for the work. This shows that official approval enhances the utility of the hila.

Source Text

The need for a lawyer for the Shar'i committee. The second work related to acting upon the issue mentioned in this book is that in this regard, establish contact with lawyers and consult them whether the case proceedings are in accordance with or against government law. We have only explained the issues so that objections against religion may be clarified. If no part of this present work applies to the importance of giving legal shape to the government decision, then influential persons should strive to get this work legally approved. There will be great reward.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage outlines a practical step for implementing the hila (legal stratagem) presented in the book. The author advises forming a Shar'i committee and consulting lawyers to ensure that the case proceedings comply with government law. This reflects an awareness of the need for external legal validation. The author also encourages influential individuals to seek official legal recognition for the work to maximize its benefit.

Key Terms
وکلاء (wukala): Lawyers or legal representatives who can advise on compatibility with government law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
For a hila to be practically effective, the mufti must integrate shar'i rulings with legal compliance through consultation with lawyers.

Giving Women the Right to Divorce in Hanafi Marriage
Introducing the first part on women's right to talaq at marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the legal stratagem (hila) that gives a woman the right to divorce in Hanafi fiqh and explain its basis.

Core Idea
A woman can obtain the right to divorce in Hanafi marriage through delegation (tafwid) or conditional talaq (ta'liq) — a valid legal stratagem.

This lesson introduces the first part of a discussion on giving women the right to divorce at the time of marriage in Hanafi fiqh. The author sets the context by highlighting the difficulties women face today, paving the way for a legal stratagem (hila) that allows women to secure this right within the marriage contract. Understanding this stratagem is essential for modern fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
What difficulty does the passage highlight? The author points to the hardships women face after marriage in contemporary times.
2
Recognize the need for a hila
Why is a special stratagem needed? In Hanafi fiqh, the right to talaq is normally exclusive to the husband; a hila is needed to grant this right to the wife without violating core principles.
A hila is a permissible legal device to achieve a legitimate end.
3
Understand the legal basis
The stratagem relies on delegation (tafwid) or conditional talaq (ta'liq) at the time of marriage. These are valid contracts based on mutual consent.
Delegation and condition are standard contract mechanisms in Hanafi law.
4
Note the objective
The goal is to give women a right they do not inherently possess, empowering them within the bounds of the sacred law.

Source Text

First part - Discussion in Hanafi fiqh of giving women the right to divorce at the time of marriage. Question: In today's era, the extent of difficulties that women face after marriage...
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of a new section in the work, titled 'First Part: Discussion on Giving Women the Right to Talaq at the Time of Marriage in Hanafi Fiqh.' The author poses a practical question about the hardships women face after marriage in contemporary times, setting the stage for presenting a legal stratagem (hila) that allows women to secure the right to divorce within a Hanafi marriage contract. This is a common theme in later Hanafi fatwa works addressing modern needs.

Key Terms
طلاق کا حق (talaq ka haqq): The legal right of a woman to initiate divorce, typically delegated by the husband at the time of marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Women can be granted the right to divorce in Hanafi marriage through delegation (tafwid) or conditional talaq (ta'liq), which are valid legal stratagems.

Tafwid al-Talaq: Delegating Divorce to the Wife via Marriage Conditions
Question-answer on tafwid al-talaq via kabin nama conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the validity of tafwid al-talaq in Hanafi fiqh and identify the key conditions for its enforceability.

Core Idea
A wife can be given the right to divorce herself (tafwid al-talaq) via a valid stipulation in the marriage contract.

This lesson examines a pressing contemporary issue: how can a woman protect herself from a failing marriage when no Islamic court is available? The Hanafi school provides a legal stratagem (hila) through tafwid al-talaq, where the husband delegates his right of divorce to his wife under specific conditions. The passage we study presents a question about the validity of such conditions in the marriage document (kabin nama) and begins to outline the ruling. By the end, you will understand the foundational ruling and the conditions that make this delegation effective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem Context
Read the questioner's description of women's hardships: lack of maintenance, abandonment, impotence, forced marriage, etc. This sets the stage for the need of a hila.
The author mentions absence of a proper shari' court as a key factor.
2
Locate the Proposed Hila
The questioner asks about a 'treatment' (علاج): writing conditions in the kabin nama that give the wife the right to divorce herself (تفویض طلاق). Identify this as tafwid al-talaq.
The answer affirms its validity and begins to discuss conditions.
3
Note the Hanafi Basis
Understand that in Hanafi fiqh, the husband can delegate his right of divorce (tafwid) to the wife. This is a valid exercise of his right, not a transfer of ownership.
The delegation must be clear and unconditional (or conditioned on specific events).
4
Consider Timing Variations
The questioner asks whether the conditions must be written before, during, or after the marriage contract. The answer in the passage is cut off, but we know from Hanafi sources that conditions placed at the time of nikah (as part of the contract) are most secure.
A condition after nikah may require the husband's separate consent.
5
Recognize the Incomplete Answer
The passage ends mid-sentence. For full details on conditions, one must consult complete texts like 'Al-Hilat al-Najijah' or standard fatwa collections.
This lesson covers only the concept and initial ruling; additional research is needed.

First Part - Discussion on giving women the right to divorce at the time of marriage in Hanafi fiqh. Question: In today's era, the difficulties women face after marriage need no explanation. Sometimes the husband treats her with oppression and displeasure, neither provides maintenance nor gives divorce. Sometimes the husband becomes indifferent to wife and children and goes abroad. Sometimes the husband proves impotent. Sometimes an orphan girl's marriage is [forced] in an unsuitable place against her will. Sometimes the husband develops insanity, etc. If there were a shari' judiciary in India, all such problems would be easy to solve. But since a shari' qadi is not present, women face severe hardship. If they file a case in court to dissolve the marriage, sometimes a non-Muslim judge decides the case, which is not legally enforceable, and sometimes a Muslim judge decides but due to ignorance of rulings does not abide by shari' law, so that decision is also unsatisfactory. Thus it is asked from scholars. [Question:] The treatment suggested in some places for these problems is that at the time of marriage, conditions be written in the kabin nama from the husband that give women the right to effect divorce upon themselves when needed. Is this legally correct and valid? If it is valid, what is its condition? Is it permissible? [2] Is there any difference between having the kabin nama written before marriage, after marriage, or having the conditions stated orally at the time of the marriage contract? Answer: (1) Having such a kabin nama written in which the right of divorce is placed in the hand of the wife and using it when needed [is...]
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage begins a discussion on a hila (legal stratagem) in Hanafi fiqh: giving the wife the right to divorce (tafwid al-talaq) by stipulating conditions in the marriage contract (kabin nama). The author sets the context of widespread difficulties faced by women due to absent or ineffective shari' courts. The questioner asks whether including such conditions is valid, what the conditions are, and whether timing (before, during, or after the contract) matters. The answer begins but cuts off: it affirms that writing such a kabin nama placing the right of divorce in the wife's hand is permissible, subject to conditions. The rest of the answer is not included in the scanned pages. This stratagem is based on the Hanafi principle of tafwid (delegation of divorce), which allows a husband to delegate the right of divorce to his wife under specific terms. The authority weight is from later Hanafi fatwa literature (Fatawa/Mutakhkhirin).

Key Terms
تفویض طلاق (tafwīḍ al-ṭalāq): The husband's delegation of the right to issue divorce to the wife.
کابین نامہ (kābīn nāmah): Marriage contract document; in the subcontinent, often includes stipulated conditions.
حیلہ شرعیہ (hīlah sharʿiyyah): A legal stratagem permissible under Shari'ah to achieve a legitimate goal while complying with the law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Invalid, because divorce is only the husband's right.
B) Permissible, but with conditions to be clarified.
C) Valid only if written before the marriage contract.
D) Valid only if the wife is illiterate.

Key Takeaway
Tafwid al-talaq — delegating divorce to the wife via marriage conditions — is a valid and practical Hanafi hila for protecting women in the absence of a shari' court.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate
6 min
Validity of Delegating Divorce to Wife via Marriage Contract
Fatwa on delegating divorce to wife via marriage contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a valid delegation of divorce (tafwid al-talaq) in a marriage contract, ensuring that the condition includes idafa (linkage to the marriage) as required by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Delegating divorce to the wife is valid only when the delegation is explicitly linked to the marriage (idafa).

In cases of marital oppression where the husband neglects or abandons his wife without divorcing her, the Hanafi school permits a legal stratagem (hila): including a condition in the marriage contract that gives the wife the right to divorce herself. However, this delegation (tafwid) is not automatically valid; it requires a specific link to the marriage contract. This lesson examines the ruling and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem and the hila
The passage describes situations of marital harm (oppression, lack of maintenance, desertion, impotence) without access to a shari'ah judge. The proposed remedy is to write conditions in the marriage contract that delegate the power of divorce to the wife.
This hila is called tafwid al-talaq.
2
Name the three permissible scenarios
The author states three forms: writing the condition before marriage, stating it orally at the time of marriage, or writing it after marriage. All three are ja'iz.
Second scenario includes oral conditions during the marriage ceremony.
3
Locate the condition for scenarios 1 and 2
For pre-marriage and at-marriage delegation, a crucial condition is that the delegation must contain idafa (linkage) to the marriage. The clause must explicitly refer to the future marriage, e.g., 'If I marry so-and-so...'
Without this linkage, the delegation is void.
4
Apply the condition to a sample clause
Draft a valid clause: 'If I marry [her name] and then violate condition X, she has the right to divorce herself.' Contrast with an invalid clause lacking marriage reference.
Example of invalid: 'If I fail to provide maintenance, my wife is divorced.'
5
Check the source authority
The passage cites Tanwir al-Absar and Fatawa Alamgiri. These are later Hanafi texts, but the ruling is consistent with earlier usul.
Authority level: fatawa mutakhkhirin.

ا۔ بعض جگہ ان مشکلات کا یہ جو علاج تجویز کیا گیا ہے کہ نکاح کے وقت شوہر سے کا بین نامہ میں اس قسم کی شرائط لکھوالی جائیں جن کی وجہ سے خواتین کو بوقت ضرورت اپنے اوپر طلاق واقع کرنے کا اختیار حاصل ہو جائے یہ شرعا صحیح اور معتبر ہے یا نہیں ؟ اگر ان سے تواس کے کانوں کے معتبر ہی کی شر کیا ہے؟ جائز ہے -۲- کیا اس کا بین نامہ کو نکاح سے قبل اور نکاح کے بعد لکھوانے یا عین عقد نکاح کے وقت شرائط کو زبانی کہلانے میں کوئی فرق ہے ؟
الجواب
(۱) اس قسم کا " کا بین نامہ تحریر کرانا کہ جس میں طلاق کا اختیار عورت کے (بیوی کے ہاتھ میں دے دیا گیا ہو اور بوقت ضرورت اس سے کام لینا شرعا جائز ہے اور اس قسم کے اختیار دینے کو تفویض طلاق کہتے ہیں اور شرائط کا بیان ا مندرجہ ذیل ہے جو کہ نمبر ۲ میں مذکور ہے۔
(۲) اس کی تہنوں صورتیں جائز ہیں خواہ نکاح سے قبل لکھوایا جائے ۔ ۲۰ چاہتے عین وقت عقد میں زبان سے کہلوایا جائے بہتے خواہ بعد میں لکھوایا جائے۔ لیکن پہلی اور دوسری صورت کے میچ دمعتبر ہو نے کی ایک ایک شرط ہے۔ عورت کو طلاق کا حق سپرد کرنے کی بحث پہلی صورت یہ ہے کہ کا بین نامہ سے پہلے لکھا جائے اس کے معتبر اورمفید ہونے کے لیے یہ شرط ہے کہ اس میں نکاح کی طرف افضا و نسبت موجود ہو۔ در کابین نامہ کا مضمون یہ ہونا چاہیئے کہ اگر میں فلاں دختر کابین نامہ کا مضمون فلاں کے ساتھ نکاح کروں اور پھر اقرار نامہ میں مذکور شرائط میں سے کسی شرط کے خلاف کروں تو مسماة مذکور کو اختیار ہو گا کہ اُس وقت یا پھر کسی وقت چاہے تو عورت خود پر ایک بائن طلاق واقع کر کے اس کے نکاح سے الگ ہو جائے ۔ اگر اس میں نکاح کی جانب اضافت نه تحریر کی گئی تو یہ اقرار نامه محض بیکار ہوگا اس کی رو سے عورت کو کسی قسم کا اختیار حاصل نہ ہوگا ۔
لما في تنوير الابصار باب التعليق وشرطه الملك كقوله لمنكوحة ان زهبت فانت طالق او الاضافة اليه كان نكحتك فانت طالق خلفا قوله الاجنبية ان زرت زيرا فانت طالق الخ شامي ص ٢٣ - وفي الفصل الثالث من كتاب الشروط للعالمكيرية ما نصه والثاني تعليق التفولين بالشرط وانه اقسام الى ان قال القسم الثاني تعليق التفويض نبرك نقد المعجل الى وقت كذا صورة كتابت هذا القسم جعل أمرها بيدها
He is not in need of explanation. Sometimes a man (husband) treats his wife with oppression and dissatisfaction, neither providing food and maintenance nor divorcing her. Sometimes the husband becomes carefree of wife and children and goes away. Sometimes the husband proves impotent. Sometimes an orphan girl's marriage is given to an unsuitable place and the girl dislikes it. Sometimes the husband becomes afflicted with insanity, etc. If there existed a shari'ah qadi in India, the remedy for all such troubles would be easy. But when no shari'ah qadi exists, women face severe hardship. If they file a case in court to dissolve the marriage, sometimes a non-Muslim judge decides the matter, which is not valid shari'ah; sometimes a Muslim judge decides but due to unfamiliarity with laws does not decide in accordance with shari'ah, so that decision is also unsatisfactory. Hence it is asked from the scholars:
1. Is this remedy proposed in some places, that at the time of marriage conditions be written in the 'kabin nama' such that women may obtain the authority to effect divorce upon themselves when needed, valid and reliable in shari'ah? What are its conditions if it is valid? Is it permissible? 2. Is there any difference between writing the kabin nama before marriage, after marriage, or having the conditions spoken orally at the time of marriage?
Answer:
(1) To write such a 'kabin nama' in which the authority of divorce is given into the wife's hands and to use it when needed is permissible in shari'ah. Giving such authority is called 'tafwid talaq'. The conditions will be stated below in number 2.
(2) All three forms are permissible: whether written before marriage, or spoken orally at the time of marriage, or written after marriage. But the first and second forms have one condition for being valid and beneficial. The discussion of granting the wife the right of divorce: the first form is that it be written before marriage. For it to be valid and beneficial, the condition is that it contain reference (idafa) and relation to the marriage. The content of the kabin nama should be: 'If I marry such and such daughter...' and then if I go against any condition mentioned in the agreement, then the said woman shall have the authority that she may effect one ba'in divorce upon herself at that time or later and separate from his marriage. If reference to marriage is not written in it, then this agreement will be completely useless; the wife will not obtain any authority from it.
From Tanwir al-Absar, chapter of Ta'liq, its condition is kingship like saying to one's wife 'if you go then you are divorced' or reference to it like 'if I marry you then you are divorced' contrary to his statement about a non-mahram woman 'if you visit Zaid then you are divorced' etc. [From] Shamai p.23. And in the third chapter of Kitab al-Shurut of Alamgiri: its text: 'The second is ta'liq tafwid...' until 'the second section: ta'liq ta'wid... to such time. The form of writing this section: placing her affair in her hand.'
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a legal stratagem (hila) for women facing marital oppression without access to a shari'ah qadi. The problem is that husbands may mistreat, neglect, or abandon wives without divorcing them, and women have no effective remedy. The solution proposed is to include conditions in the marriage contract (kabin nama) that delegate the power of divorce to the wife. The author confirms that this is valid (ja'iz) in the Hanafi madhhab and is called 'tafwid al-talaq' (delegation of divorce). The passage then lists three permissible scenarios: writing the conditions before marriage, stating them orally at the time of marriage, or writing them after marriage. However, for the first two scenarios (before or at the time of marriage), a crucial condition is added: the delegation must be linked (mudaf) to the marriage. That is, the condition must be phrased in a way that refers to the future marriage, e.g., 'If I marry so-and-so...'. Without this linkage, the agreement is void. The text cites Tanwir al-Absar and Fatawa Alamgiri to support this. The citation from Tanwir al-Absar explains that ta'liq (suspension) of divorce requires either current ownership of the wife (i.e., already married) or a reference to future marriage. A statement to an unrelated woman (ajnabiyya) like 'If you visit Zaid, you are divorced' is invalid. Thus, the hila is valid only when properly constructed.

Key Terms
تفویض طلاق (tafwid al-talaq): Delegating the authority to divorce to the wife by the husband, enabling her to issue divorce upon herself under stipulated conditions.
اضافت (idafa): Linking the conditional divorce to the marriage, i.e., explicitly referring to the marriage in the condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the essential condition for the validity of a delegation of divorce (tafwid talaq) written before the marriage contract?
A) The writing must be witnessed by two male witnesses
B) The condition must be linked to the marriage by referring to the future marriage
C) The husband must say 'I give you authority' orally
D) The wife must accept the delegation immediately

Key Takeaway
Delegating divorce to the wife is a permissible Hanafi stratagem, valid only when the condition contains a clear link to the marriage (idafa) for pre-marriage or at-marriage delegation.

Conditions for Valid Tafwid al-Talaq
Explains two forms of delegating divorce and their conditions for validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two valid forms of tafwid al-talaq and state the essential condition for each form's validity.

Core Idea
Tafwid al-talaq requires explicit linkage to marriage — without it, the delegation is void.

This passage explains the legal stratagem (hila) known as tafwid al-talaq, where the husband delegates the right of divorce to the wife. Two forms are presented: a written agreement before marriage and a verbal stipulation during the marriage contract. The key to validity is proper linkage to the nikah. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, draws on authoritative Hanafi sources to clarify the conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two valid forms
Recognise that tafwid al-talaq can be done either in writing before the nikah or verbally during the marriage contract. Each has its own condition.
2
Condition for the written pre-marriage form
The agreement must explicitly link the delegation to the future marriage (e.g., 'If I marry you... and I violate a condition, you may divorce yourself'). Without this linkage (idafah ila al-nikah), the document is void.
Refer to the passage: 'اس میں نکاح کی طرف افضا و نسبت موجود ہو'
3
Condition for the verbal form during contract
The offer (ijab) must come from the wife or her representative, stating conditions and that she retains the right to divorce herself upon breach. The husband must accept (qabul). The wife's acceptance of the delegation must occur in the same session (majlis al-tafwid).
The passage says: 'ایجاب عورت کی جانب سے ہو'
4
Appreciate the third form from Alamgiriyya
The text also mentions a ta'liq of delegation by condition, such as husband's failure to pay advanced dower. This is a variation where the delegation is suspended on a future condition.
This further illustrates the flexibility of the hila within Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text

(۲) اس کی تہنوں صورتیں جائز ہیں خواہ نکاح سے قبل لکھوایا جائے۔ ۲۰ چاہتے عین وقت عقد میں زبان سے کہلوایا جائے بہتے خواہ بعد میں لکھوایا جائے۔ لیکن پہلی اور دوسری صورت کے میچ دمعتبر ہو نے کی ایک ایک شرط ہے۔ عورت کو طلاق کا حق سپرد کرنے کی بحث پہلی صورت یہ ہے کہ کا بین نامہ سے پہلے لکھا جائے اس کے معتبر اورمفید ہونے کے لیے یہ شرط ہے کہ اس میں نکاح کی طرف افضا و نسبت موجود ہو۔ در کابین نامہ کا مضمون یہ ہونا چاہیئے کہ اگر میں فلاں دختر کابین نامہ کا مضمون فلاں کے ساتھ نکاح کروں اور پھر اقرار نامہ میں مذکور رائط میں سے کسی شرط کے خلاف کروں تو مسماة مذکور کو اختیار ہو گا کہ اُس وقت یا پھر کسی وقت چاہے تو عورت خود پر ایک بائن طلاق واقع کر کے اس کے نکاح سے الگ ہو جائے۔ اگر اس میں نکاح کی جانب اضافت نه تحریر کی گئی تو یہ اقرار نامه محض بیکار ہوگا اس کی رو سے عورت کو کسی قسم کا اختیار حاصل نہ ہوگا۔
لما في تنوير الابصار باب التعليق وشرطه الملك كقوله لمنكوحة ان زهبت فانت طالق او الاضافة اليه كان نكحتك فانت طابق خلفا قوله الاجنبية ان زرت زيرا فانت طالق الخ شامي ص ٢٣ - وفي الفصل الثالث من كتاب الشروط للعالمكيرية ما نصه والثاني تعليق التفولين بالشرط وانه اقسام الى ان قال القسم الثاني تعليق التفويض نبرك نقد المعجل الى وقت كذا صورة كتابت هذا القسم جعل أمرها بيدها في تعليقه واحدة بائنة مطلقاً بشرط نه اذا مضى شهر اولد كن او آخره كذا ولم يوود اليها جميع ما قبل تعجيلة لها من صداقتها وهو كذا فانها تطلق نفسها بعد ذالك منى شأت ابدا واحدة بائنة فوق الأمد في ذالك ابها وانها قبلت منه هذا الأمر فى مجلس التفويض القسم الثالث تعليق التقولين بشرط تمارو او بشرب الخمر أو ضربه ضرباً مرجعا يظهر اثره على بدنها وصورة كتابته على نحو ما بيناه - رعالمگیری مصری ملت جمل)
قلنا قوله وانها قبلت في مجلس التفويض قد خرج معزج عادة المحاضر والسجلات والانتبولها في مجلس التكلم وقوع الشرط كما سيأتي وقد صرح بذالك في الفصل الأول من الباب الثالث.
اور دوسری صورت کہ مین ایجاب وقبول ہی میں کا بین نامہ میں مذکور شرائط بزبان شرائط مذکور ہوں اس کے صحیح ومعتبر ہونے کی شرط یہ ہے کہ ایجاب عورت کی جانب سے ہو یعنی اولاً خود عورت یا اس کا دلی یعنی قاضی نکاح خوان عقد نکاح کے وقت اس طریقہ سے کہے کہ میں نے اپنے آپ کو یا مسماۃ فلاں بنت فلاں کو اس شرط پر تمہارے نکاح میں دے دیا کہ اگر تم نے یہ کام کیا یادہ کام کیا اس قدر شرائط لگانا مقصود ہو وہ سب شرطیں لگا دی جائیں تو اپنے معاملہ کا اختیار میرے یا سماء موصوفہ کے ہاتھ میں ہو گا یعنی شرائط مذکورہ میں سے کسی ایک شرط کی خلاف ورزی پر بھی اختیار ہوگا کہ اسی وقت یا پھر کسی وقت چاہوں یا چاہے تو اپنے آپ کو ایک طلاق ا بائن دے کر اس نکاح سے الگ کر سکوں گی دبا کر سکے گی اس کے جواب میں نکاح کرنے والا شخص اس طریقہ سے کہے کہ میں نے قبول
[1] It is permissible, and this type of giving authority is called 'tafwid al-talaq' (delegation of divorce). Its conditions are given below in number 2. [2] Three forms are permissible: whether it is written before marriage, or spoken at the time of the contract, or written after marriage. But for the first and second forms to be valid, each has a condition. Discussion of handing over the right of divorce to the woman: The first form is that it is written before the marriage document (kabin nama). For it to be valid and effective, the condition is that it must be linked and referred to the marriage. The content of the marriage document should be: 'If I marry such-and-such daughter... and then I violate any of the conditions mentioned in the agreement, then the said woman will have the option, at that time or at any later time, if she wishes, to effect one irrevocable divorce upon herself and separate from the marriage.' If the linkage to the marriage is not written, this agreement becomes utterly useless; the woman will have no authority whatsoever by virtue of it. As in Tanwir al-Absar, chapter of Ta'liq: its condition is that he has ownership (of the wife), like his saying to his wife 'if you go, you are divorced' or linkage to it, like 'if I marry you, you are divorced' – unlike his saying to a foreign woman 'if you visit Zaid, you are divorced' etc. (Radd al-Muhtar, p.23). And in the third chapter of the Book of Conditions in al-Fatawa al-Alamgiriyya: 'The second is ta'liq of delegation by a condition, and it has divisions... until he said: the second division is ta'liq of delegation by leaving the advanced dower until a certain time. The form of writing this division: putting her affair in her hand in one irrevocable divorce, with the condition that if a month passes... and he does not pay her the advanced dower... then she may divorce herself after that, whenever she wishes, one irrevocable divorce... and that she accepted this order from him in the council of delegation. The third division: ta'liq of divorce by a condition of repudiation, or drinking wine, or beating her severely...' We say: his statement that she accepted in the council of delegation has come out in the custom of minutes and records, and they pay attention to it in the council of the occurrence of the condition, as will come later, and this is explicitly stated in the first chapter of the third part. And the second form [mentioned in the Urdu]: In the offer and acceptance itself, the conditions mentioned in the marriage document are stated verbally. For it to be correct and valid, the condition is that the offer be from the woman's side, i.e., first the woman herself or her representative (the marriage officiant) says at the time of the marriage contract in this manner: 'I have given myself or the said daughter of so-and-so into your marriage on the condition that if you do this or that... all conditions being stipulated, then the authority of my affair is in my hand or the said woman's hand' – i.e., upon violation of any one condition, she has the option either immediately or later, if she wishes, to give herself one irrevocable divorce and separate from this marriage. In response, the man accepting the marriage says in this manner: 'I have accepted.'
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal stratagem (hila) known as tafwid al-talaq, where the husband delegates the right of divorce to the wife. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, explains two valid forms of such delegation and their conditions. The first form is a written agreement before the marriage contract (kabin nama). For it to be valid, the agreement must explicitly link the delegation to the upcoming marriage; without this linkage, the agreement is void. The second form occurs during the marriage contract itself, where the wife (or her representative) makes the offer (ijab) stipulating that she retains the right to divorce herself if certain conditions are breached. The husband must then accept (qabul). The author supports this with references from Hanafi fiqh texts: Tanwir al-Absar, Radd al-Muhtar, and al-Fatawa al-Alamgiriyya. These sources confirm that delegation requires ownership (i.e., marriage) or a direct link to it. The passage emphasizes that the wife's acceptance of the delegation must occur in the same session (majlis) for it to be binding. This is a classic Hanafi hila to resolve situations where the husband wishes to give the wife a measure of control over the marriage without violating the principle that divorce is the husband's prerogative.

Key Terms
تفویض طلاق (tafwid al-talaq): Delegation of the right of divorce by the husband to the wife, conditional upon the occurrence of marriage or a specific condition.
تعلیق التفویض (ta'liq al-tafwid): Suspending the delegation of divorce upon a condition, e.g., husband's failure to pay dower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first form of tafwid al-talaq (written before marriage), what is the essential condition for the agreement to be valid?
A) The agreement must be witnessed by two male witnesses.
B) The agreement must explicitly link the condition to the future marriage (e.g., 'If I marry you...').
C) The wife must sign the agreement herself.
D) The husband must have paid the mahr in full.

Key Takeaway
The validity of tafwid al-talaq hinges on explicit linkage to marriage and proper acceptance in the council.

Tafwid al-Talaq: Comparing Legal Stratagems for Delegating Divorce
Presenting multiple scenarios for tafwid al-talaq with conditions and best practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a valid tafwid al-talaq, compare three scenarios (pre-marriage deed, wife-initiated offer, post-marriage pledge), and apply the safest method in a fatwa context.

Core Idea
The safest hila for tafwid al-talaq is a pre-marriage deed explicitly referencing the future marriage; without this reference, the deed is void.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's work presents a detailed discussion of legal stratagems (hiyal) for delegating the right of divorce to the wife in the Hanafi school. The author examines multiple scenarios, weighing their validity and practicality. By understanding the conditions and pitfalls of each method, you will be able to advise women seeking this protection and issue sound fatwas on the matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The text describes three ways to delegate divorce: (1) pre-marriage kabin nama with condition, (2) wife-initiated offer with husband adding condition in acceptance, (3) post-marriage iqrarnama. Note the author's evaluation of each.
The scenarios vary in reliability and mutual consent requirements.
2
Understand the principle of idafah (reference to marriage)
For the pre-marriage deed to be valid, it must explicitly refer to the future marriage. Without idafah, the deed is void. Highlight the importance of this condition.
This is a key fatwa point: the condition must tie the divorce to the marriage.
3
Analyze the wife-initiated offer scenario
If the wife offers without the delegation condition, and the husband adds it in acceptance, the delegation becomes valid after marriage. However, the husband retains discretion, making it unreliable for the wife.
This relies on the principle that the response (jawab) repeats the question (su'al).
4
Evaluate the post-marriage iqrarnama
Obtaining a written pledge after marriage is valid but depends entirely on the husband's consent. It offers no unilateral protection for the wife.
This method is not recommended for those seeking guaranteed authority.
5
Apply the tarjih (preferred position)
The author concludes that the first scenario (pre-marriage kabin nama with idafah) is the easiest and safest. This is the mufta bihi position for fatwa issuance.
The preference is based on avoiding ambiguity and ensuring the wife's right is secured before the marriage contract is finalized.

And similarly it is stated in [Fatwa] Alamgiri 23. Between the jurists, Abu al-Layth found a distinction between the two forms: he said because the initiation (al-bada') if it is from the husband, then the divorce and delegation (al-tafwin) is before marriage, so it is not valid. But if it is from the woman, then delegation (al-taqwid) occurs after marriage, because when the husband after the woman's speech said 'I accept' - and the response includes rephrasing the question, it becomes as if he said 'I accept on the condition that you are divorced' or 'on the condition that the matter is in your hand', so it becomes delegated after the nikah. [Reference from] al-Shami, Book of Divorce, under the verse: 'And the divorce of a master over the wife of his slave does not occur unless he says' [etc.] [Urdu:] Further discussion related to delegating the right of divorce to the wife: If the offer is from the wife's side, but the condition of delegating the right of divorce to the wife was not delegated, and the husband in acceptance added the condition of delegation of the right, even then delegating the right of divorce to the wife becomes correct. 150 But because in this case the husband has the option whether to add the condition or not, since the wife's offer without any condition has already been given, the matter has been concluded from his option. For this reason, for a woman whose aim is to obtain the authority to take divorce, this form is not sufficient; rather, it is necessary to stipulate the condition in the offer so that the husband does not have the right to accept without condition, even if this form is rare; it has been written for general benefit. Yes, if before the husband's acceptance, the wife or her guardian etc. get the idea and add the condition of ta'wil [delegation], then the man has the right to accept that condition. It remains not. The third form of delegating the right of divorce to the wife: And the third form is that after marriage, a written pledge (iqrar nama) is obtained from the husband in this manner; this form is also valid and absolutely correct. This form is useful for that woman who did not take a kabin nama in the marriage, i.e., whose marriage was written without a kabin nama. But for a woman who wants caution at the time of marriage, this also has the same deficiency that was mentioned above: when the marriage is complete, it is no longer in her control to force the husband to write such a pledge; rather, the matter depends solely on the husband's consent. Therefore, for the distressed woman, the best solution for obtaining relief is to take a kabin nama from the husband before marriage, adopting the first or second form. Among them, the easy method in which there is no risk of common people falling into error is only the first form: the kabin nama is written before marriage. But in that, it is necessary to include a reference to marriage. That is, in the kabin nama, the husband should be made to write these words: 'If I marry so-and-so daughter of so-and-so and then do contrary to such-and-such conditions etc., (then my wife is irrevocably divorced).' And if the reference to marriage is not made in the kabin nama, then the kabin nama will be invalid, as has been explained before. And Allah, Glorious and Exalted, knows best.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage presents a hila (legal stratagem) discussion from the Hanafi school regarding delegating the right of divorce (tafwid al-talaq) to the wife. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, begins by citing a distinction made by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi between two scenarios: if the offer of delegation comes from the husband before marriage, it is invalid because divorce cannot be effective before marriage; but if it comes from the wife, the delegation can be effective after marriage because the husband's acceptance (qabul) can be reinterpreted to include the condition of delegation. The author then addresses a specific scenario in Urdu: if the wife makes an offer without explicitly stipulating the right of divorce, and the husband in his acceptance adds that condition, the delegation still becomes valid. However, this relies on the husband's discretion; therefore, it is not reliable for a woman seeking guaranteed authority. The better method is for the woman to explicitly stipulate the condition in her offer. The third scenario is obtaining a written pledge (iqrar nama) from the husband after marriage. This is valid but depends entirely on the husband's willingness, giving the woman no unilateral power. The author concludes that the safest and easiest method is the first: to have a kabin nama (marriage deed) written before marriage that includes a conditional divorce clause with explicit reference to the marriage. This ensures the woman's right without ambiguity. The passage emphasizes that without referencing the marriage in the deed, the kabin nama is void. The authority weight is from later Hanafi fatwa works (usul al-iftā'), combining principles from Shami and Fatwa Alamgiri. The text illustrates the practical application of the Hanafi maxim 'al-umūr bi maqāṣidihā' (matters are judged by intentions) through the conditionality of the offer.

Key Terms
تفویض (tafwīḍ): Delegation of authority, specifically the right to divorce, from husband to wife.
کابین نامہ (kābīn nāmah): A written marriage contract deed that specifies the dower and conditions, used here for including delegation of divorce.
اقرار نامہ (iqrār nāmah): A written pledge or acknowledgment, here a document from the husband post-marriage agreeing to delegate divorce.
ایجاب (ījāb): Offer, the proposal made by one party in a contract.
قبول (qabūl): Acceptance, the response that concludes the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which scenario is the most recommended and safe for a woman to secure the right of divorce?
A) Obtaining a written pledge (iqrar nama) after marriage.
B) Having a pre-marriage kabin nama with an explicit condition of delegation and reference to the marriage.
C) Making an oral offer without any written document.
D) Asking the husband to add the condition during acceptance after the marriage contract.

Key Takeaway
The safest Hanafi hila for tafwid al-talaq is a pre-marriage kabin nama with an explicit condition of delegation and a clear reference to the marriage; without the reference, the deed is void.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate

Distinction Between Nikah Mu'allaq and Nikah Mashrut
Explains the difference between suspended and conditional marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a suspended marriage (nikah mu'allaq) and a conditional marriage (nikah mashrut) and apply the Hanafi rule to determine validity.

Core Idea
Suspended marriage is void; conditional marriage is valid with a binding stipulation.

This passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah clarifies a critical distinction that often causes confusion. A marriage contract that is conditioned upon a future event (mu'allaq) is not concluded at all, while a marriage that is concluded immediately but includes an additional condition (mashrut) is valid under Hanafi law. Understanding this difference is essential for correctly applying marriage contracts and for constructing valid legal stratagems.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of marriage
Read the passage and note the two categories: nikah mu'allaq (suspended) and nikah mashrut (conditional).
The author uses examples to illustrate each.
2
Determine the hukm for each type
From the text, the hukm for mu'allaq is that the marriage is not concluded (invalid). For mashrut, the marriage is concluded immediately and the condition is binding.
3
Analyze the example of mu'allaq
Consider the woman's statement: 'If my father consents, I have given myself in marriage.' Explain why this is suspended and therefore invalid.
The contract depends on a future event, so no immediate effect.
4
Analyze the example of mashrut
The text states that if a condition is added without suspending the original marriage, the marriage is valid with the condition. Explain the difference.
The contract session completes the marriage; the condition is an extra stipulation.
5
Note the Hanafi position and opposition
Identify that some scholars mistakenly consider any condition as making the marriage suspended, but the Hanafi view distinguishes based on the effect on the contract.
The Hanafi view is relied upon.

مذکورہ بالا نکاح کہ جس میں شوہر سے معلق نکاح اور مشروط نکاح میں فرق کچھ شرا [؟] منظور کر لی گئی ہیں جنفیہ کے نزدیک اس کے جائز ہونے میں شبہ نہیں ہے بعض حضرات نے اس صورت کو نکاح معلق میں داخل کر کے شہید کیا ہے لیکن حقیقت ہیں یہ نکاح معلق نہیں بلکہ نکاح ہجزہ ہے جو کہ معلق تفویض کے ساتھ مشروط ہے، نکاح معلق وہ ہے کہ اس وقت نکاح ہی نہ ہو۔ جیسے کہ کوئی عورت اس طرح کہے کہ اگر میرے والد رضامند ہوں تو میں نے خود کو تمہارے نکاح میں دے دیا ، یا شوہر اس طریقہ سے کہے کہ اگر میرے والد ( اس نکاح سے ) رضامند ہوں تو میں نے قبول کر لیا تو اس صورت میں نکاح منعقد نہیں ہوتا۔ اور اگر اصل نکاح معلق نہ کیا جائے بلکہ اس کے ساتھ کوئی زائد شرط لگا دی جائے تو اس طریقہ سے نکاح منعقد ہو جاتا ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہوتا ہے کہ مجلس عقد میں نکاح اُسی وقت ہو رہا لیکن اس کے ساتھ ایک شرط ہے جس کو شوہر سے تسلیم کرایا جاتا ہے۔
چونکہ خواتین ناقص العقل ہوتی ہیں اس وجہ سے حق طلاق مطلقاً ان کے اختیار میں دے دینا شطرہ سے خالی نہیں ہے حق اس وجہ سے مناسب یہ ہے کہ عورت کو طلاق کا حق سپرد کرنے کی صورت میں کوئی مناسب قید کا اضافہ کر دیا جائے جس میں وہ خطرہ نہ رہے مثلاً یہ کہ نکاح کے وقت عورت کی جانب سے وہ خود یا اُس کا ولی یا وکیل یعنی قاضی نکاح خواں اس طریقہ سے کہے کہ میں نے خود کو یا مسماۃ فلاں ، دختر فلاں کو تمہارے نکاح میں بعوض مہر ---- بسکہ رائج الوقت اسی شرط کے ساتھ دے دیا کہ جس وقت اُس کو تم سے کسی قسم کی شدید تکلیف پہونچے گی جس کو خلا اشخاص میں سے کم سے کم دو حضرات تسلیم کر لیں اس جگہ مناسب یہ ہے کہ کم سے کم دس افراد کے نام فریقین کی رضامندی سے متعین کر دیئے جائیں اس کے بعد معاملہ کے وقت میرے یا اس کے اختیار میں ہو گا کہ خود پر ایک بائن طلاق واقع کرے کہ اس نکاح سے علیحدگی اختیار کر لی جائے اس صورت کا اختیار عورت کو اُس وقت حاصل ہو گا جبکہ تسلیم کردہ حضرات میں سے دو حضرات تسلیم کرلیں کہ واقعی تکلیف شدیدہ ہے دینی شوہر نے بیوی کو تکلیف شدید پہنچائی ہے تو اس صورت میں نکاح کے وقت جو کا بین نامہ شوہر سے تحریر کرایا گیا ہے اس کے مطابق وہ دو حضرات توریت پر طلاق بائن واقع کر سکتے ہیں)
تفویض طلاق کے لیے ایک ضروری ہدایت اس کے باوجود عورت کو بھی چاہیے کہ طلاق واقع کرنے میں محجبلت سے کام نہ لے بلکہ اطمینان سے غور کر کے قدم اٹھائے اور تین باتوں کا ضرور النترام کرتے۔ ایک ضروری مشورہ پہلی بات یہ ہے کہ فور حصہ (یا نارنگی کے وقت اس اختیار ریعنی تفوین طلاق) سے کام نہ لے بلکہ ایک معتقد به العینی مناسب مرت ) تک خور و فکر کرے جس کی میعاد ایک ہفتہ سے کم نہ ہو۔ دوسرے یہ کہ اپنے خیر خواہوں سے مشورہ کرے ۔ تیسرے یہ کہ سنت کے موافق استعمارہ کرے اور دعا بھی کرے کہ اسے خدا میرا دل ایسے کام کی جانب پھیر دے جو کہ میرے لیے دین، دنیا میں بہتر ہو اس تمام کوشش کے بعد جو کچھ دل میں آئے اُس پر عمل کرے اور خداوند قدوس پر اعتماد رکھے اس طریقہ پر وہ خطرہ نہیں ہو گا جو کہ عورت کو حق طلاق سپرد کرنے کی صوت میں حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ واللہ اعلم
The above-mentioned marriage (nikah) regarding the difference between suspended and conditional marriage. Some conditions have been accepted; there is no doubt about its permissibility according to the Hanafis. Some people have considered this as a suspended marriage and have refuted it, but in reality it is not suspended; rather it is a conditional marriage which is conditioned upon delegation of divorce. Suspended marriage is that where the marriage itself does not occur at that time. For example, if a woman says, 'If my father consents, I have given myself in marriage to you,' or the husband says, 'If my father consents (to this marriage), I have accepted,' then in such a case the marriage is not concluded. But if the original marriage is not suspended, rather an additional condition is attached to it, then in this manner the marriage is concluded. The result is that in the contract session the marriage takes place at that very time, but there is a condition which is imposed upon the husband. Since women are deficient in intellect, giving absolute right of divorce into their hands is not free from risk. Therefore, it is appropriate that when entrusting the right of divorce to the woman, an appropriate restriction should be added so that there is no risk. For example, at the time of marriage, on behalf of the woman, she herself or her guardian or her agent, i.e., the marriage officiant (qazi nikah khwan), says in this manner: 'I have given myself (or so-and-so woman, daughter of so-and-so) in marriage to you in lieu of the customary dower on this condition that when she suffers severe hardship from you, which at least two persons from among the appointed persons recognize.' At this point, it is appropriate that at least ten persons be appointed by mutual consent of the parties. Thereafter, at the time of the matter, it will be in the option of me or her to effect a single irrevocable divorce upon herself to separate from this marriage. The woman will have this option only when two of the appointed persons recognize that indeed severe hardship has occurred, i.e., the husband has caused severe harm to the wife. Then, according to the written agreement obtained from the husband at the time of marriage, those two persons can effect an irrevocable divorce by attestation. A necessary instruction for delegation of divorce: Despite this, the woman should also not act hastily in effecting divorce, but should step forward with calm deliberation, and must adhere to three things. One necessary advice: First, she should not use this option (i.e., delegation of divorce) immediately or at the time of anger, but should reflect and ponder for a moderate appropriate period, the duration of which should not be less than one week. Second, she should consult her well-wishers. Third, she should perform istikhara according to the Sunnah and also pray that God turn my heart towards such action which is better for me in religion and world. After all this effort, she should act upon what comes to her heart and rely on the Holy God. In this way, there will not be the risk that is incurred in the case of giving the absolute right of divorce to the woman. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a hila (legal stratagem) from the book Al-Hilatul Najijah. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, addresses the issue of granting the wife the right to divorce (tafwid al-talaq) in a manner that avoids legal and social risks. First, he distinguishes between two types of conditional marriage: 'nikah mu'allaq' (suspended marriage) and 'nikah mashrut' (conditional marriage). In a suspended marriage, the actual contract is made contingent upon a future event, and the marriage does not take place until that event occurs. For example, if a woman says, 'I marry you if my father consents,' no marriage contract is formed because the offer is suspended. In contrast, a conditional marriage is concluded immediately in the contract session, but a condition is attached that must be fulfilled. The author then explains why giving the woman absolute right to divorce is risky due to women's emotional nature (mentioned as 'naqis al-aql' – deficient in intellect, a common legal characterization). To mitigate this risk, he proposes a hila: at the time of marriage, the wife (or her agent) stipulates that if she suffers severe harm from the husband, and at least two agreed-upon persons confirm it, she has the right to effect a single irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in). The condition requires that at least ten impartial persons be named by mutual consent, and two of them must verify the harm. This ensures that the divorce is not frivolous. Finally, the author advises the woman to not act hastily, but to wait at least a week, consult others, perform istikhara, and rely on Allah. This entire passage is a practical legal stratagem rooted in Hanafi jurisprudence, using the principle of 'shart' (condition) to regulate the delegation of divorce.

Key Terms
نکاح معلق (nikah mu'allaq): A marriage contract that is made contingent upon a future event; the contract is not valid until the event occurs. Example: 'I marry you if my father agrees.'
نکاح مشروط (nikah mashrut): A marriage concluded immediately but with an additional condition that must be fulfilled; the contract is valid and the condition is binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between a suspended marriage (nikah mu'allaq) and a conditional marriage (nikah mashrut)?
A) Both are invalid; there is no difference.
B) In suspended marriage, the contract is not concluded at the moment; in conditional marriage, it is concluded immediately with a condition.
C) In conditional marriage, the contract is suspended; in suspended marriage, it is immediate.
D) Both are valid but conditional marriage requires a witness from the husband's side.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates a marriage concluded immediately with an additional condition, but invalidates a marriage that is suspended upon a future event.

Hila for Tafwid al-Talaq: Delegating Divorce with Safeguards
Presents a hila for tafwid al-talaq with conditions and safeguards.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a valid Hanafi legal stratagem (hila) for delegating the right of divorce to the wife, including the necessary conditions and procedural safeguards.

Core Idea
A conditional delegation of divorce with appointed arbiters prevents misuse and is a valid hila.

This passage presents a practical hila (legal stratagem) to safely delegate the right of divorce to the wife. The author acknowledges the risk of giving absolute divorce power to women due to emotional impulsivity, and therefore proposes a structured mechanism: the wife is granted the right to effect a single irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) only when two appointed persons confirm severe hardship. Additionally, the wife must follow a week-long deliberation, consultation, and istikhara. This lesson unpacks the conditions and procedures of this hila, which is a model for responsible tafwid al-talaq in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem and solution
Read the passage to understand the risk of giving absolute divorce power to the wife and the proposed solution: a conditional delegation with external verification.
The risk is described as the woman being 'naqis al-aql' (deficient in intellect) – a legal characterization, not a personal judgment.
2
Extract the core condition
Find the central condition: the wife can only divorce when two appointed persons confirm she has suffered severe hardship (shiddat takleef).
3
Outline the appointment of arbiters
Note that at least ten persons are to be mutually agreed upon by the parties, and any two of them can certify the hardship.
This ensures objectivity and prevents hasty decisions.
4
Identify the procedural safeguards for the wife
Extract the three steps: wait at least one week, consult well-wishers, perform istikhara and prayer.
These safeguards are meant to ensure the divorce is not impulsive.
5
Understand the hila's validity
The author asserts that with these conditions, the risk of misuse is eliminated, and the hila is valid per Hanafi law.
The reliance is on Allah; the hila is a practical tool.

تفویض طلاق کے لیے ایک ضروری ہدایت اس کے باوجود عورت کو بھی چاہیے کہ طلاق واقع کرنے میں محجبلت سے کام نہ لے بلکہ اطمینان سے غور کر کے قدم اٹھائے اور تین باتوں کا ضرور النترام کرتے۔ ایک ضروری مشورہ پہلی بات یہ ہے کہ فور حصہ (یا نارنگی کے وقت اس اختیار ریعنی تفوین طلاق) سے کام نہ لے بلکہ ایک معتقد به العینی مناسب مرت ) تک خور و فکر کرے جس کی میعاد ایک ہفتہ سے کم نہ ہو۔ دوسرے یہ کہ اپنے خیر خواہوں سے مشورہ کرے ۔ تیسرے یہ کہ سنت کے موافق استعمارہ کرے اور دعا بھی کرے کہ اسے خدا میرا دل ایسے کام کی جانب پھیر دے جو کہ میرے لیے دین، دنیا میں بہتر ہو اس تمام کوشش کے بعد جو کچھ دل میں آئے اُس پر عمل کرے اور خداوند قدوس پر اعتماد رکھے اس طریقہ پر وہ خطرہ نہیں ہو گا جو کہ عورت کو حق طلاق سپرد کرنے کی صوت میں حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ واللہ اعلم
The above-mentioned marriage (nikah) regarding the difference between suspended and conditional marriage. Some conditions have been accepted; there is no doubt about its permissibility according to the Hanafis. Some people have considered this as a suspended marriage and have refuted it, but in reality it is not suspended; rather it is a conditional marriage which is conditioned upon delegation of divorce. Suspended marriage is that where the marriage itself does not occur at that time. For example, if a woman says, 'If my father consents, I have given myself in marriage to you,' or the husband says, 'If my father consents (to this marriage), I have accepted,' then in such a case the marriage is not concluded. But if the original marriage is not suspended, rather an additional condition is attached to it, then in this manner the marriage is concluded. The result is that in the contract session the marriage takes place at that very time, but there is a condition which is imposed upon the husband. Since women are deficient in intellect, giving absolute right of divorce into their hands is not free from risk. Therefore, it is appropriate that when entrusting the right of divorce to the woman, an appropriate restriction should be added so that there is no risk. For example, at the time of marriage, on behalf of the woman, she herself or her guardian or her agent, i.e., the marriage officiant (qazi nikah khwan), says in this manner: 'I have given myself (or so-and-so woman, daughter of so-and-so) in marriage to you in lieu of the customary dower on this condition that when she suffers severe hardship from you, which at least two persons from among the appointed persons recognize.' At this point, it is appropriate that at least ten persons be appointed by mutual consent of the parties. Thereafter, at the time of the matter, it will be in the option of me or her to effect a single irrevocable divorce upon herself to separate from this marriage. The woman will have this option only when two of the appointed persons recognize that indeed severe hardship has occurred, i.e., the husband has caused severe harm to the wife. Then, according to the written agreement obtained from the husband at the time of marriage, those two persons can effect an irrevocable divorce by attestation. A necessary instruction for delegation of divorce: Despite this, the woman should also not act hastily in effecting divorce, but should step forward with calm deliberation, and must adhere to three things. One necessary advice: First, she should not use this option (i.e., delegation of divorce) immediately or at the time of anger, but should reflect and ponder for a moderate appropriate period, the duration of which should not be less than one week. Second, she should consult her well-wishers. Third, she should perform istikhara according to the Sunnah and also pray that God turn my heart towards such action which is better for me in religion and world. After all this effort, she should act upon what comes to her heart and rely on the Holy God. In this way, there will not be the risk that is incurred in the case of giving the absolute right of divorce to the woman. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a hila (legal stratagem) from the book Al-Hilatul Najijah. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, addresses the issue of granting the wife the right to divorce (tafwid al-talaq) in a manner that avoids legal and social risks. First, he distinguishes between two types of conditional marriage: 'nikah mu'allaq' (suspended marriage) and 'nikah mashrut' (conditional marriage). In a suspended marriage, the actual contract is made contingent upon a future event, and the marriage does not take place until that event occurs. For example, if a woman says, 'I marry you if my father consents,' no marriage contract is formed because the offer is suspended. In contrast, a conditional marriage is concluded immediately in the contract session, but a condition is attached that must be fulfilled. The author then explains why giving the woman absolute right to divorce is risky due to women's emotional nature (mentioned as 'naqis al-aql' – deficient in intellect, a common legal characterization). To mitigate this risk, he proposes a hila: at the time of marriage, the wife (or her agent) stipulates that if she suffers severe harm from the husband, and at least two agreed-upon persons confirm it, she has the right to effect a single irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in). The condition requires that at least ten impartial persons be named by mutual consent, and two of them must verify the harm. This ensures that the divorce is not frivolous. Finally, the author advises the woman to not act hastily, but to wait at least a week, consult others, perform istikhara, and rely on Allah. This entire passage is a practical legal stratagem rooted in Hanafi jurisprudence, using the principle of 'shart' (condition) to regulate the delegation of divorce.

Key Terms
تفویض طلاق (tafwid al-talaq): Granting the wife the right to divorce herself, often by delegating the authority to pronounce talaq under certain conditions.
حیلہ (hila): A legal stratagem used to achieve a legitimate end without violating the rules of Shariah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) To verify the occurrence of severe hardship before the wife can divorce.
C) To act as the wife's legal guardians.
D) To decide the amount of mahr.

Key Takeaway
A valid hila for delegating divorce requires objective external verification of hardship, mutual appointment of arbiters, and personal safeguards to prevent impulsive decisions.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems

Delegation of Divorce: Conditions, Precautions, and Legal Stratagem
Hila for tafwid al-talaq with ethical and procedural guidelines

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a valid ta'liq for tafwid al-talaq using precise wording and assess the ethical obligations of the wife before exercising delegation.

Core Idea
Delegation of divorce requires precise wording: 'idha' restricts to the sitting, 'idha shaa' grants perpetual right—neither is ideal without precaution.

This lesson unpacks a detailed legal stratagem (hila) from Ashraf Ali Thanwi for a woman facing severe marital hardship. We will examine the delegation mechanism, the required ethical precautions, and the crucial distinction between conditional phrases that either limit or eternalize the delegated right. By the end, you will be able to apply these principles when advising on or drafting a valid divorce delegation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem and the hila structure
Recognize that the hila addresses severe hardship (shiddat) by placing divorce in the hands of arbitrators or the wife, but only after a written agreement from the husband at the time of nikah.
The hila is a lawful way to escape harm without violating Shari'ah.
2
Specify the conditions for delegation
Note the minimum of ten appointed arbitrators with mutual consent, and that the wife's option becomes active only after two arbitrators confirm the severe hardship.
The arbitrators pronounce a ba'in divorce, not the wife directly.
3
Recognize the threefold ethical precaution
The wife must (1) wait at least one week, (2) consult well-wishers, and (3) perform istikhara before acting on the delegation.
This prevents hasty decisions and ensures the divorce is for valid reason.
4
Analyze the ta'liq wording: 'idha' vs 'idha shaa'
Using 'idha' (when) restricts the delegation to the sitting in which the condition occurs; using 'idha shaa' (whenever she wants) gives a perpetual right even after remarriage until three divorces are exhausted.
The author advises a middle wording that avoids both restriction and perpetuity.
5
Apply the hadith warnings on divorce
The passage cites two hadith: divorce is the most disliked permissible act, and a woman who seeks divorce without cause is deprived of Paradise. These reinforce the need for caution.
These warnings apply even when delegation is permitted.

مذکورہ بالا تعلیق میں اگر چاہے تعلیق خلاق سے تعلق ایک ضروری ہدایت کا لفظ استعال کرنا چاہیے ورنہ یہ تفویض خاص اس مجلس کے ساتھ مقید ہو جائے گی جس میں وہ شرائط واقع ہوں اور اس مجلس کے ختم ہونے کے بعد عورت کو طلاق کا اختیار باقی نہیں رہے گا، اور اختیار کو اس قدر محدود کر دینا ، مناسب نہیں ، اسی طرح لفظ "جب کبھی چاہے" بھی شرط میں استعمال نہ ہونا چاہیے ورنہ رایسی عورت پر ہمیشہ کے لیے (یہاں تک کہ نکاح کے اعادہ کے بعد بھی) اُس کو اپنے اوپر طلاق واقع کرنے کا اختیار رہے گا، جب تک کہ تین طلاق پوری نہ ہو جائیں ، اور اس قسم کا اختیار عورت کو دینا ضرورت سے زائد اور مصلحت کے خلاف ہے بلکہ اس قسم کے الفاظ استعمال کرنے چاہیں کر جن سے ہو تو اس قسم کی تنگی لازم آتے کہ عورت کو طلاق کا حق مجلس کے ساتھ مقید ہو عند الله سخت ناپسندیده شتی : شرعا طلاق میں جلدی کرنا نا پسند یدہ ہے حضرت رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا ہے کہ حق تعالیٰ کے نزدیک مباح (جاتہ) چیزوں سب سے زیادہ ناپسندہ طلاق ہے (ابو داؤد شریف ) نیز ارشاد نبوی ہے کہ جو گورت بلا ضرورت اپنے شوہر سے طلاق مانگے اس پر جنت کی خوشبو حرام ہے ۔ رواہ احمد تریزی، ابوداؤد ، ابن ماجہ ، دارمی ۔ عا یہ حکم اس صورت میں ہے جبکہ عورت نے اُس شرط کے پائے جانے کو خود دیکھا ہواں اگر رویت یہ عذر کرے کہ مجھ کو اس خبر پر اطمینان نہیں ہوا تھا تو اس میں تفصیل ہے وقت ضرورت شامی جارت مسائل مشتی ملاحظہ فرمائیں ۔ عہ اس کو تنبیہ کا جت اس واسطے بنا یا گیا ہے کہ جب بھی کا لفظ استعمال کرنے سے اعادہ نکاح کے بعد بھی ان می شرائط کی پابندی ضروری ہے گی اگر جری کی بنا پر نو بین شرائط میں سے کسی شرط کو موقوف کرنا چاہیں تو یہ ہو کے کئی مومند
From among the persons, at least two should affirm. In this place, it is appropriate that at least ten individuals be appointed with the consent of both parties. Thereafter, at the time of the matter, it will be in my or her option to effect one ba'in divorce upon herself to separate from this marriage. This option will be available to the woman only when two of the affirmed persons affirm that indeed severe hardship is present—that the husband has caused severe hardship to the wife. Then, in accordance with the written agreement taken from the husband at the time of marriage, those two persons can pronounce a ba'in divorce upon tawriya(?). [Followed by] An essential instruction for delegation of divorce: Despite this, the woman should not act hastily in effecting divorce but should proceed with calm deliberation and must observe three things: [1] Do not use this option (i.e., delegation of divorce) immediately at the time of anger; rather, deliberate for a suitable period, the term of which should not be less than one week. [2] Consult with well-wishers. [3] Perform istikhara according to the Sunnah and also pray that Allah turn my heart towards that action which is better for me in religion and world. After all this effort, act upon whatever comes to heart and trust in Allah. By this method, the risk that occurs in giving the right of divorce to the woman will not be present. And Allah knows best. Concerning the above-mentioned ta'liq, if one wishes, one should use the word 'idha' (when) for ta'liq related to khula'; otherwise, this delegation will be restricted to the specific sitting in which those conditions occur, and after that sitting ends, the woman will have no remaining right to divorce. To restrict the option to such a degree is not appropriate. Similarly, the phrase 'whenever she wants' should not be used in the condition; otherwise, the woman will forever have the right to effect divorce upon herself (even after renewal of marriage) until three divorces are completed. Giving such an option to the woman is beyond necessity and contrary to expediency. Rather, one should use such words that neither cause this restriction (that the woman's right to divorce is tied to the sitting) nor [cause perpetual right]. It is severely disliked in the sight of Allah: Hastening in divorce is disliked in Shari'ah. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Among the permissible things, divorce is the most disliked to Allah Almighty.' (Abu Dawud). Also, the prophetic saying: 'Any woman who asks her husband for divorce without necessity, the fragrance of Paradise is forbidden for her.' (Ahmad, Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, Darimi). And this ruling is when the woman herself has seen the occurrence of the condition. If she excuses that she was not satisfied with the news, there is detail: see Shami, etc., at the time of need. And this warning is made so that when using the word 'whenever', after renewal of marriage, the conditions are still binding. If due to some reason they wish to suspend some condition, then this can be done in some way [?]
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed hila (legal stratagem) for a woman facing severe marital hardship. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, outlines a mechanism by which the right to divorce can be delegated either to arbitrators or to the woman herself under strict conditions. The key points are: (1) Appoint at least ten mutually agreed arbitrators; (2) The arbitration panel confirms severe harm; (3) The husband's prior written consent (at the time of nikah) authorizes the arbitrators to pronounce a ba'in divorce. Thanwi then emphasizes that the woman must not act impulsively: she must wait at least a week, consult others, perform istikhara, and pray for guidance. This prevents hasty decisions that might lead to regret. Further, he discusses the precise wording of the ta'liq (conditional delegation). Using 'idha' (when) restricts the right to the sitting in which the condition occurs; using 'idha shaa' (whenever she wants) grants a perpetual right even after remarriage. The latter is excessive and against maslahah. He cites hadiths showing that divorce, though permitted, is severely disliked by Allah, and that a woman who seeks divorce without cause is deprived of Paradise. Finally, he notes that if the woman herself witnesses the condition (e.g., harm), she may act; if she relies on news, further details from Shami apply. This entire passage exemplifies the Hanafi approach of providing lawful solutions while strictly avoiding abuse.

Key Terms
تفویض طلاق (tafwid al-talaq): Delegation of the right to divorce to the wife or a third party, conditional upon specific circumstances.
تعلیق (ta'liq): A conditional suspension of divorce, where the divorce becomes effective upon occurrence of a stipulated condition.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately without possibility of revocation; the couple cannot remarry without a new nikah.
استخارہ (istikhara): A prayer seeking guidance from Allah when making a decision, especially recommended before undertaking a significant act like divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One day
B) Three days
C) One week
D) One month

Key Takeaway
Delegation of divorce is a valid Hanafi hila for severe hardship, but it requires precise wording and ethical precautions to avoid abuse and regret.

Stratagem: Conditional Divorce on Remission of Mahr
Author presents a legal stratagem for conditional divorce with mahr remission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct and explain the Hanafi hila for conditional divorce with mahr remission, identifying its conditions and legal consequences.

Core Idea
A conditional tafwid tied to ibra ensures the divorce only occurs if the wife remits the mahr.

This passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah presents a practical stratagem for a husband who desires a divorce but wishes to secure the wife's forfeiture of the mahr. The hila uses the mechanism of conditional delegation (tafwid mu'allaq), where the wife is empowered to divorce herself only if she first remits the dower. Understanding its conditions and legal consequences is essential for muftis drafting marital settlements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal objective
The husband wants to divorce his wife while also ensuring she gives up her right to the mahr. This is a common situation where the wife is unwilling to divorce without compensation.
2
Recognize the mechanism
The hila uses tafwid al-talaq (delegation of divorce) conditioned on ibra' (remission of mahr). The wife becomes an agent to pronounce divorce upon herself, but only after she has remitted the mahr.
The condition makes the agency effective only upon fulfillment.
3
Examine the wording
The husband writes in the kabinnama: 'Remitting the mahr, I pronounce upon myself a ba'in divorce.' Alternatively, he says: 'Three divorces are in your hand if you remit my mahr from your mahr.' The precise phrasing ties the divorce to the remission.
The wording must clearly link the condition to the agency.
4
Analyze the quoted ruling
The text states: if she remits and then divorces, the divorce occurs; but if she divorces without remitting (voluntarily), the divorce does not occur because the agency was conditioned on remission.
This protects the husband: he only gets the divorce if she forfeits the mahr.
5
Extract the conditions of validity
The hila requires: (1) the wife must be given agency, (2) the agency must be conditional upon her remitting the mahr, (3) the remission must be express and before the divorce, (4) the wife must pronounce the divorce after remission, (5) the husband must not revoke the agency before the condition is fulfilled.
These conditions ensure the hila is legally effective.

Source Text

Divorcing on the condition of remission of mahr: A beneficial thing for the husband is that he should place the condition of remission of mahr for giving divorce. If this condition is agreed upon, then the way to implement it is that in the marriage contract, before the sentence 'I pronounce one ba'in divorce on myself', these words should be written: 'Remitting the mahr, I pronounce upon myself... (a ba'in divorce).' He said to her: 'Three divorces are in your hand if you remit my mahr from your mahr' up to his saying: 'If she presents the remittance, it occurs, but if she voluntarily [gives] without being asked, it does not occur because the agency was conditioned upon remittance.' - From him.
