Commentary
This passage presents a hila (legal stratagem) for a husband who wants to divorce his wife but also wants her to forfeit her mahr (dower). The stratagem works by combining two elements: (1) The wife pronounces a ba'in divorce upon herself, but (2) she does so on the condition that she first remits the mahr. In practice, the kabinnama wording should include a clause where the wife says, 'Remitting the mahr, I pronounce one ba'in divorce on myself' before the standard phrase. The author then quotes a ruling: If the husband says, 'Three divorces are in your hand if you remit my mahr from your mahr,' then if she remits and divorces, it takes effect; but if she divorces without remitting (e.g., voluntarily giving up mahr without it being a condition), the divorce does not occur because the agency (tawkili) was expressly tied to the condition of ibra (remission). This ensures the husband's goal: he gets the divorce only if she releases the mahr. The passage is a practical tool for Hanafi jurists drafting marriage contracts.

Key Terms
ابراء مہر (ibra' mahr): Remission or forgiveness of the dower (mahr) by the wife, typically in exchange for something (here, divorce).
حیلہ (hila): A legal stratagem or device that achieves a permissible objective through indirect means, while staying within the boundaries of Shariah.
تفویض (tafwid): Delegation of the power to divorce to the wife by the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A conditional tafwid al-talaq tied to ibra' mahr ensures the divorce only takes effect if the wife first remits the dower, protecting the husband's financial interest.

Sample Marriage Deed with Conditional Talaq Delegation
Provides a sample marriage deed with conditional talaq delegation and practical advice for muftis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a valid marriage deed (kabin nama) that includes conditional delegation of talaq, applying Hanafi conditions, and evaluate the recommended practice.

Core Idea
A wife can receive conditional talaq delegation, but absolute discretion is discouraged to prevent misuse.

This passage presents a practical legal stratagem (hila) from the Hanafi tradition: a marriage deed that allows the wife to pronounce an irrevocable divorce if the husband breaks specific conditions. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, provides a sample deed and then advises caution, recommending a more restricted version. Understanding this hila equips you to draft valid conditions that balance legal enforceability with responsible delegation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
Determine what issue this hila addresses: the wife's lack of recourse if the husband breaches agreed conditions.
The hila empowers the wife via conditional talaq delegation.
2
Extract structural elements
List the key components: parties, dower, conditions, delegation clause.
The deed must clearly state the conditions and the wife's right.
3
Analyze the conditional delegation
Examine how the husband delegates talaq: conditional upon violation, with option for immediate or future use.
The wife pronounces one irrevocable divorce (talaq-e-bain).
4
Examine the author's caution
Understand why the author advises against absolute delegation: risk of hasty divorce.
He recommends a restricted version with witness confirmation.
5
Distinguish the two versions
Compare unrestricted vs. restricted: the latter requires two witnesses to confirm violation before the wife can act.
This balances validity with sadd al-dhara'i'.

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. ... I (son of ... caste resident of district ...) am a resident of ... My marriage with the named (daughter of ... caste resident of district ...) has been fixed on the following conditions with a dower of ... rupees of current coin. Therefore, I, in full possession of my senses and without any coercion, write the following declaration so that I remain bound by it, and if there is non-compliance, the said Muslim woman may have a way to release herself. I declare that as long as she remains in my marriage, I will abide by the following conditions. And for the sake of assurance, I write that if I marry the said woman and after marriage violate any of the following conditions, then the said woman shall have the option to immediately or at any time, if she wishes, to pronounce one irrevocable divorce (talaq-e-bain) upon herself and separate from this marriage. The conditions are as follows. I have approved this deed and after writing and reviewing it, I sign it today dated ... Witnessed, Witnessed. When setting conditions, it is appropriate to consult experienced knowledgeable people, and also lawyers whether these conditions are valid legally, and it is also appropriate to get this deed registered. In the aforementioned deed, only this much has been observed that it becomes Shariah-compliant and valid, but according to it, once a condition is violated, the woman gets absolute power of one divorce. Under the heading of necessary advice, we have written before that giving absolute power to the woman is not appropriate. For this reason, another clause is also written so that the person who wants to act on this necessary advice may have the deed written in this manner.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage presents a legal stratagem (hila) in the form of a marriage deed (kabin nama). The author provides a sample deed where the husband, at the time of marriage, undertakes to abide by certain conditions and gives his wife the power to pronounce a single irrevocable divorce if he violates any condition. This is a valid conditional delegation of talaq (tafwid al-talaq bi al-shart) according to Hanafi fiqh. However, the author then advises that giving such absolute power to the wife is not recommended (khilaf al-awla), as it may be used impulsively. Therefore, he introduces a second, more restricted version where the violation is confirmed by two witnesses before the wife's right to divorce is triggered. The passage illustrates the Hanafi approach of using contractual conditions to protect women's rights while cautioning against potential misuse.

Key Terms
کابین نامہ (kabin nama): A marriage contract deed that records the dower and any conditions agreed upon by the parties.
طلاق بائنہ (talaq-e-bain): An irrevocable divorce that immediately ends the marriage without possibility of revocation or remarriage without a new contract.
شرائط (shara'it): Conditions stipulated in the marriage contract that, if violated, trigger a remedy such as delegation of divorce.
تفویض الطلاق بالشرط (tafwid al-talaq bi al-shart): Conditional delegation of divorce, where the husband gives the wife the right to divorce herself upon the occurrence of a specified condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A valid marriage deed can include conditional talaq delegation, but the recommended Hanafi practice requires witness confirmation to prevent misuse.

The Suspended Marriage Deed: A Hila for Conditional Divorce with Witness Verification
Provides a modified marriage deed with witness verification condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the mechanism of the suspended marriage deed (hila) and identify its key condition: witness verification before the wife's right to divorce is activated.

Core Idea
The suspended deed ensures the wife's right to divorce is verified by witnesses, preventing misuse.

This passage presents a refined legal stratagem (hila) for marriage deeds. The author modifies a previous version by requiring that at least two specified men confirm the husband's violation before the wife can exercise her delegated right to divorce. This addresses the problem of the wife having absolute and potentially impulsive power. In Hanafi fiqh, such conditional delegations are permissible as long as the condition is clear and not contrary to Shariah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core problem the hila addresses
The original unconditional delegation gave the wife immediate right to divorce, which could be misused. The hila introduces a safeguard.
2
Extract the new condition added
Find the phrase requiring at least two of the mentioned persons to confirm the violation. This is the suspended condition.
The phrase is 'کم سے کم دو آدمی تسلیم کر لیں'
3
Explain how the condition modifies the original deed
The wife's right is no longer absolute; it depends on an external verification step. This slows the process and reduces abuse.
4
Note the incomplete ending and intended completion
The passage ends abruptly; the likely completion specifies that the witnesses must be named in the deed and that their acknowledgment triggers the right.
The author probably intended to write the witness names and the final clause.
5
Relate to Hanafi principle of conditional talaq and istihsan
Hanafi school allows conditional talaq provided the condition is clear and not against Shariah. This hila uses that principle via istihsan to achieve a balanced outcome.
Istihsan (juristic preference) permits this modification for public benefit.

This passage presents an improved legal stratagem (hila) for the marriage deed. Conditional Marriage Deed: Two Types and Hanafi Application
Explains two types of conditional marriage deeds and provides sample text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a valid conditional marriage deed (mu'allaq kabin nama) by distinguishing between the two types and applying Hanafi conditions for valid stipulations.

Core Idea
A conditional marriage deed should grant the wife a limited, time-bound right to divorce to avoid Shariah conflicts.

This passage presents a practical legal stratagem (hila) for wives to protect their rights by including conditions in the marriage contract. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, explains two types of conditional deeds: one that grants permanent divorce authority upon any breach, and another that limits the option to a one-month window per breach. This lesson explores the differences and the drafting considerations, including the role of witnesses and legal consultation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
Carefully read the passage to distinguish the first type (absolute, permanent right upon any breach) from the second type (one-month option per breach, limited to the current marriage).
The first type gives the wife a single, absolute divorce right after any violation; the second gives repeated but temporary options.
2
Understand the Shariah concern
The author advises against giving the wife absolute and permanent authority because it may lead to instability or abuse. The second type is presented as a more balanced solution.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that stipulations in marriage must not contradict the marriage's purpose (e.g., permanence with flexibility).
3
Examine the sample draft
Look at the draft provided. Note the conditional language: 'if I violate any condition... then the wife has the option to divorce herself... within one month of acknowledgment.'
The draft includes a clause requiring at least two witnesses to confirm the breach, adding a layer of verification.
4
Apply the marginal notes
The marginal notes recommend appointing at least ten witnesses to ensure availability, adding a clause for witnesses to deem separation appropriate, and consulting lawyers to confirm legal recognition.
These notes emphasize practical enforceability, a key concern in iftaa.
5
Distinguish the practical consequence (thamarah)
The key difference is that the first type gives a one-time permanent option, while the second gives repeated one-month windows. The latter is preferable as it preserves the marriage while providing recourse.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is the second type due to its moderation.

دونوں کا بین نامر میں فرق

(بقیہ حاشیہ) کم سے کم (دس آدمیوں کے نام دونوں فریق کی رضامندی سے تقریر کئے جائیں کیونکہ دو، چارافراد کے نام لکھنے میںممکن ہے کہ ضرورت کے وقت اُن میں سے کوئی بھی موجود نہ رہے اور زیادہ افراد میں اس قسم کا احتمال مشکل ہے ۔
(۲) اگر زیادہ ضرورت محسوس ہو تو کا بین نامہ تسلیم کر لینے کے بعد اس جملہ کا بھی اضافہ کردیا جائے اور وہ دونوں حضرات، عورت کے لیے علیحدگی مناسب بھی قرار دیں ۔ (۳) کابین نامہ لکھواتے وقت) جو شرائط مقرر ہوں ان میں معاملہ فہم اور تجربہ کار حضرات سے مشورہ کرنا مناسب ہے نیز وکلاء سے بھی مشورہ کرنا چاہیئے کہ جو شرائط کا بین نامہ میں لکھوائی ہیں وہ قانون میں تسلیم ہیں یا نہیں؟ اوراگ کا مبین نام کی تیاری کر لی جائے تو بہتر ہے۔
In the aforementioned marriage deed, only this consideration was given that it should be permissible and valid in Shariah, but accordingly, after one violation of a condition, the woman will obtain absolute right to one divorce. And under the heading of necessary advice, we have written before that giving the woman absolute right is not appropriate. Therefore, another subject is also written so that whoever wishes to act on this necessary advice may have a marriage deed written in this way. Draft of the conditional marriage deed: In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. I, son of... district... caste... resident of... country... are, my marriage with the named woman, daughter of..., caste..., resident of..., district..., has been established on the following conditions with a mahr of [unclear] rupees [unclear] coins. Therefore, I write this declaration with sound mind and without coercion or duress so that I remain bound to it, and in case of non-compliance with conditions, there may be a way of release for the said woman. So I declare that as long as she remains in my marriage, I will remain bound to the following conditions, and I write for satisfaction: If I marry the said woman and after marriage I violate any of the following conditions, and at least two men from the mentioned persons acknowledge the violation, then it is appropriate that at the time of marriage, when the husband is made to write the marriage deed, at this place [remainder of marginal note?]. Thereafter, the said woman will have the option that at that time or within one month from the acknowledgment of the violation, whenever she wishes, she may effect one irrevocable divorce upon herself and separate from this marriage. And whenever a condition is violated, every time the woman will have the option for one month. But this option is limited to this one marriage. If after separation she wishes to remarry by some means, then thereafter this option and conditions do not apply; rather, whatever is agreed upon again will be acted upon. These are the conditions. Difference between the two marriage deeds: The difference between the first marriage deed mentioned above and the second marriage deed is that after writing the first marriage deed, once the husband acts against a condition, the woman gets the right to divorce herself permanently. Then if the husband [continues]. (Remainder of marginal note) At least ten men's names should be appointed with the consent of both parties, because in writing two or four individuals, it is possible that at the time of need none of them may be present, and with more individuals such a possibility is rare. (2) If greater need is felt, after accepting the marriage deed, this sentence may also be added, and those two gentlemen should also consider separation appropriate for the woman. (3) While having the marriage deed written, it is appropriate to consult with sensible and experienced persons regarding the conditions to be set, and also to consult with lawyers whether the conditions written in the marriage deed are recognized in law. And it is better if the marriage deed is prepared in advance.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage discusses a type of legal stratagem (hila) in marriage contracts, specifically a conditional marriage deed (mu'allaq kabin nama). The author first notes that an earlier simple deed gave the wife absolute and permanent right to divorce upon breach of any condition, but he now advises against such absolute right. Instead, he presents a second type where the wife's right to divorce is limited to one month after each breach, and this right only applies to the current marriage; if the marriage is renewed, new conditions may be set. The difference between the two types is that in the first, one breach gives permanent option; in the second, each breach gives a one-month window, and repeated breaches give repeated but not permanent options. The author also provides a sample draft of the conditional deed and includes marginal notes advising to appoint at least ten witnesses to avoid absence issues, to add a clause giving witnesses discretion to deem separation appropriate if needed, and to consult experienced persons and lawyers to ensure the conditions are legally recognized. This reflects the Hanafi concern for practical and enforceable legal stratagems that avoid future disputes.

Key Terms
کا بین نامہ (kabin namah): A marriage deed or contract that records the terms of marriage, including mahr and conditions.
معلق (mu'allaq): Conditional; here it refers to a kabin nama where the wife's right to divorce is contingent upon the husband's breach of conditions.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that immediately terminates the marriage and cannot be revoked without a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key difference between the first and second types of conditional marriage deeds described in this passage?
A) In the first type, the wife gets one divorce per breach; in the second, she gets two divorces.
B) In the first type, the wife gets a permanent and absolute right to divorce after one breach; in the second, she gets a one-month option after each breach.
C) In the first type, the husband retains the right to divorce; in the second, the wife has the right.
D) In the first type, the wife must go to court; in the second, she can divorce herself.

Key Takeaway
The conditional marriage deed should grant the wife a limited, time-bound right to divorce to avoid Shariah violations.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate
8 min
Two Types of Kabin Namah and Judicial Separation
Explains two types of kabin namah and lists grounds for tafriq shar'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of kabin namah, distinguish their differences in duration of the wife's option, and list the five grounds for judicial separation mentioned in the text.

Core Idea
The wife's delegated right to divorce is limited to one marriage; judicial separation is restricted, prompting the author to adopt Maliki law for four grounds.

This passage introduces a practical legal stratagem (hila) used in South Asian Hanafi contexts: the kabin namah, a marriage contract that gives the wife a conditional right to divorce herself. Two types are described, differing in how long the wife keeps her option after a violation. The passage then shifts to judicial separation (tafriq shar'i), listing five grounds but noting that only impotence is handled according to Hanafi fiqh; the remaining four are taken from Maliki fiqh. This reflects the author's pragmatic blending of madhhabs for resolving modern family law issues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of kabin namah
Read the passage to find the description of the first and second types. Note that the first gives a perpetual option after the first violation, while the second gives a one-month option per violation.
The first type: upon any violation, the wife gains an indefinite right to divorce herself. The second: each violation gives a one-month window.
2
Distinguish the duration of the option
Compare the duration: in the first type, the wife can exercise her option at any future time after the first violation; in the second type, the option must be exercised within one month of each violation.
After exercising the option and divorcing, the option is not revived if the couple remarries.
3
Note the common limitation
Both types share a limitation: once the wife actually divorces (talaq ba'in), any remarriage does not revive the conditions or options. The delegation ends with the marriage.
The husband's violations only matter within the current marriage.
4
List the five grounds for judicial separation
The passage lists five causes for tafriq shar'i: impotence (عنین), insanity (مجنون), missing husband (مفقود), recalcitrant husband (متعنت), and absent non-missing husband (غائب غیر مفقود).
The author specifies that the first cause (impotence) is treated under Hanafi fiqh; the rest are from Maliki fiqh.
5
Recognize the madhhab blending methodology
Notice that the author uses Maliki fiqh for four grounds because Hanafi law is restrictive on judicial separation. This is a talfiq or combined approach for practical fatwa.
This methodology is often used by later Hanafi jurists to address modern needs.

دوسرا حصہ
حاکم شرعی کے فیصلہ کی وجہ سے شوہر بیوی کے درمیان تفریق شرعی
یہ حصہ مندرجہ ذیل اسباب کی بناء پر تفریق شرعی طلاق واقع ہونے پر طے ہے۔
1- عنین (نامرد) کی بیوی کا حکم 2- مجنون شخص کی بیوی کا حکم 3- مفقود (بالکل لاپتہ شوہر کی بیوی کا حکم 4- متعنت (یعنی بیوی کے حقوق سے لاپرواہ شخص) کی بیوی کا حکم 5- غائب غیر مفقود (یعنی ایسا شخص جس کے زندہ ہونے کا یقین ہو اور وہ پردیس وغیرہ جاکر غائب ہوگیا ہو) کی بیوی کا حکم
(ایک دلیل از فقہ حنفی و بقیه از فقه مالکی)
مذکورہ بالا تفریق شرعی کے اسباب میں سے پہلا سبب یعنی عنین کی بیوی کی کس طرح تفریق واقع کی جائے، یہ ستار فقہ حنفی کی رو سے ذیل میں بیان کیا جاتا ہے، اور بقیہ یعنی زوجہ مجنون، زوجہ مفقود، زوجہ حاضر متعنت، زوجہ غائب غیر مفقود کے احکام فقہ مالکی کی رو سے پیش کیے جاتے ہیں۔
After that, the mentioned woman will have the option that at that very time or within one month from when she acknowledges the violation of the condition, then whenever she wishes, she may effect one irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) upon herself and separate from this marriage. And whenever there is a violation of the condition, each time she will get the option for one month. However, this option is limited to one marriage; if after separation by any means she wishes to renew the marriage, then after that there is no option or conditions, but whatever is agreed upon anew will be acted upon accordingly. These are the conditions: ... Difference between the two kabin namahs: The difference between the first kabin namah and the second is that after writing the first kabin namah, upon the first violation of any condition, the wife gains the option to effect divorce upon herself forever. Then if the husband violates any condition... (remaining footnote) At least ten men should be appointed by mutual consent, because if only two or four are named, it is possible that none of them will be available when needed, but with more people this likelihood is remote. (2) If there is a greater need, after the kabin namah is accepted, this sentence may also be added: 'and those two gentlemen may also deem separation suitable for the wife.' (3) When writing the conditions of the kabin namah, it is appropriate to consult experienced and knowledgeable persons, and also to consult lawyers whether the conditions written in the kabin namah are recognized in law; and it is better to prepare the kabin namah in advance. ... If a violation is found on the husband's side, the wife will get the option of divorce again for one month, and every time the husband violates the condition, she will get the option in this way. But in this matter, both kabin namahs are common in that once a ba'in divorce occurs on the wife, after a subsequent marriage, the option will not be available due to violation of conditions. Second section: Judicial separation between husband and wife by the decision of a Shar'i judge. This section is based on the following causes upon which judicial separation by divorce occurs: 1- Ruling regarding the wife of a sexually impotent man. 2- Ruling regarding the wife of an insane person. 3- Ruling regarding the wife of a missing person (completely lost). 4- Ruling regarding the wife of a recalcitrant (negligent of wife's rights). 5- Ruling regarding the wife of a non-missing absent person (one known to be alive but has gone abroad and disappeared). (One proof from Hanafi fiqh and the rest from Maliki fiqh). Among the above causes of judicial separation, the first cause, i.e., how separation is effected for the wife of an impotent man, is stated below according to Hanafi fiqh. The remaining, i.e., rulings for wife of insane, wife of missing, wife of present recalcitrant, wife of absent non-missing, are presented according to Maliki fiqh.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents a hila (legal stratagem) for wives to obtain divorce through conditional delegation in the marriage contract (kabin namah). Two types are described: In the first type, upon any violation of conditions by the husband, the wife gains a perpetual option to divorce herself with one ba'in talaq at any future time. In the second type, each violation grants only a one-month window to exercise the option. Both types share a common limitation: if the wife actually divorces and later remarries the same husband, the conditions and option are not revived. The passage then introduces the second section of the work on judicial separation (tafriq shar'i) by a judge. It lists five causes, but specifies that only the first cause (impotence of husband) will be treated according to Hanafi fiqh; the remaining four causes will be treated according to Maliki fiqh. This reflects the author's methodology of combining madhhabs when necessary for practical fatwa, likely because Hanafi law is restrictive in granting judicial separation on those grounds.

Key Terms
کابین نامہ (kabin namah): A marriage contract document that includes specific conditions agreed upon by the spouses, often used to give the wife the right to divorce herself upon breach.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately; the couple cannot remarry without a new contract.
اختیار (ikhtiyar): The option or right given to the wife to pronounce divorce upon herself when conditions are violated.
تفریق شرعی (tafriq shar'i): A judicial decree of separation issued by a Shar'i judge on specific grounds such as impotence, insanity, etc.
متعنت (muta'annit): A husband who is litigious or neglects his wife's rights, causing harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second type of kabin namah described, how long does the wife have to exercise her option to divorce after a violation of conditions?
A) Indefinitely, until she dies
B) One month from the violation
C) One month from the marriage
D) One year from the violation

Key Takeaway
The kabin namah is a hila that gives the wife a conditional right to divorce, but its options are limited to one marriage; judicial separation is treated by combining Hanafi (impotence) and Maliki (other grounds) rulings.

The Hila of Delegated Divorce and Judicial Separation: Two Stratagems for Women
Explaining two types of legal stratagems for women to obtain divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for valid tafwid al-talaq and distinguish between Hanafi and Maliki grounds for judicial separation.

Core Idea
A valid hila requires clear conditions; Hanafi limits judicial separation, Maliki expands it.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilat al-Najizah offers two practical solutions for women in troubled marriages: a contractual delegation of divorce and a judge's decree of separation. Understanding the conditions and the cross-madhhab approach is essential for modern fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two legal stratagems
Recognize that the passage presents two distinct hila: (1) tafwid al-talaq (delegated divorce at marriage) and (2) tafriq shar'i (judicial separation) with five grounds.
The first is contractual; the second requires a qadi.
2
Analyze the conditions for valid tafwid
The text specifies that the wife gets an option for one month per violation, but after a ba'in divorce and remarriage the option does not revive. This limitation is critical.
Conditions must be clearly stated and accepted.
3
List the grounds for judicial separation
Five causes: impotence (Hanafi), insanity, missing husband, recalcitrance, absent but known alive (Maliki). Only the first is from Hanafi fiqh.
This mixing of madhhabs is a practical concession.
4
Compare Hanafi and Maliki positions
Hanafi allows judicial separation only for impotence; Maliki allows for several forms of harm. The author adopts Maliki for the other four due to necessity.
Understand the basis: Hanafi strictness vs Maliki harm principle.
5
Apply the fatwa hierarchy
For tafwid, Hanafi ruling is operative. For judicial separation, the mufti may follow Maliki dispensation. The practical question: conditions can be written at any time but must be clearly accepted.
The fatwa hierarchy here involves takhayyur (selecting dispensations).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

۔ قدیم نسخہ میں یہ مضمون خلاصہ الحیلہ الناجزہ کے تحت تھا موضوع کی مناسبت کے پیش نظر اس جگہ شریک اشاعت کیا گیا۔
If a violation of any condition is found on the part of [the husband], then the woman will again obtain the option of divorce for one month, and every time the husband violates the condition, the option will remain available in this manner. But in this matter, both aforementioned [parties] are mutually bound by the written agreement that once a ba'in divorce occurs upon the woman, then after remarriage she will not obtain the option due to violation of the condition. Second part: Judicial separation between husband and wife by the decree of a shar'i judge. This right is based on the following causes for judicial separation (divorce occurring): 1- Ruling for the wife of an impotent man. 2- Ruling for the wife of an insane person. 3- Ruling for the wife of a missing (completely lost) husband. 4- Ruling for the wife of a recalcitrant (i.e., neglectful of the wife's rights) person. 5- Ruling for the wife of an absent but not missing person (i.e., a person whose living is certain and who has gone abroad and become absent). (First from Hanafi fiqh, rest from Maliki fiqh). Among the aforementioned causes of judicial separation, the first cause, i.e., how judicial separation is effected for the wife of an impotent man, is explained below according to Hanafi fiqh, and the rest, i.e., rulings for the wife of an insane person, the wife of a missing person, the wife of a present recalcitrant, and the wife of an absent but not missing person, are presented according to Maliki fiqh. Summary of discussion: The summary is that 'Al-Hilat al-Najizah lil-Halilat al-'Ajizah' has two parts. First part: Delegation of divorce at the time of marriage, i.e., the ruling of the woman effecting divorce herself. Question: Today in India, due to the absence of a shar'i judge, the problems faced by women need no description. Sometimes the husband oppresses and does not fulfill the wife's rights, neither provides maintenance nor issues divorce; sometimes the husband abandons the children and disappears; sometimes the husband is not capable of the wife (i.e., is impotent); sometimes the husband is insane or mad. If a shar'i judge were present, the solution to these problems would be easy, but now the extraordinary difficulties being faced are apparent. For this reason, the question is: (a) Is the remedy that has been suggested in some places—that at the time of marriage, certain conditions of such nature be written in the marriage contract that provide women with automatic authority to effect divorce upon themselves when needed—correct and valid or not? (b) And is there any difference in having this written before the marriage, after the marriage, exactly at the time of marriage, or having these conditions stated orally? In the old edition, this content was under the summary of Al-Hilat al-Najizah; due to the appropriateness of the subject, it has been republished here.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage presents two legal stratagems (hila) for women facing difficult marriages. The first hila is tafwid al-talaq (delegated divorce) at the time of marriage: the husband delegates the power of divorce to the wife, conditional on his violation of certain agreed terms. The text clarifies that if the husband violates a condition, the wife gets the option to divorce herself within one month, and this option recurs each time the husband violates. However, if a ba'in divorce occurs and the couple remarries, the option does not revive—this is an important limitation. The second hila is judicial separation (tafriq shar'i) by a shar'i judge. The text lists five grounds: (1) impotence of husband, (2) insanity, (3) missing husband, (4) recalcitrant (neglectful) husband, and (5) absent but known alive husband. It is explicitly noted that only the first ground (impotence) is based on Hanafi fiqh; the remaining four are based on Maliki fiqh. This mixing of madhhabs is a practical solution for the current absence of a proper shar'i judiciary. The summary reiterates the two-part structure of the book 'Al-Hilat al-Najizah lil-Halilat al-'Ajizah'. Finally, the passage raises a question about the validity of writing such conditional delegations in the marriage contract, whether before, during, or after marriage, and whether orally stated. This shows the author's concern for practical fatwa in the Indian context.

Key Terms
تفویض طلاق (tafwid al-talaq): The husband's delegation of the power of divorce to the wife, usually conditioned on specific violations.
حیلہ ناجزہ (al-hilat al-najizah): An effective legal stratagem to resolve a pressing difficulty, here specifically for women unable to obtain divorce through normal means.
تفریق شرعی (tafriq shar'i): Judicial separation or divorce decreed by a shar'i judge based on specific grounds.
عنین (unnin): A man who is impotent and unable to consummate the marriage.
مفقود (mafqud): A husband who has disappeared and whose whereabouts and life status are unknown.
ممتنع (mumtani'): A recalcitrant husband who neglects the wife's rights, such as maintenance, without valid reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a husband violates a condition after the wife has received a ba'in divorce and then remarries him?
A) The wife again gets the option to divorce herself for one month.
B) The option is not revived.
C) The option becomes permanent.
D) The marriage is automatically annulled.

Key Takeaway
The combined use of tafwid al-talaq and selective adoption of Maliki grounds for judicial separation provides a comprehensive solution for women in difficult marriages.

Tafwid al-Talaq: Delegating Divorce as a Permissible Legal Stratagem
Explaining the permissibility and conditions of delegating divorce at marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a valid tafwid al-talaq and construct a fatwa on its permissibility based on Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Delegating divorce to the wife is permissible when written with precise wording to solve genuine hardships.

This passage from Thanwi's Al-Hilat al-Najizah addresses the pressing problem of Muslim women trapped in failing marriages when no Shari'ah judge is available. The author presents a legal stratagem (hilah) known as tafwid al-talaq, where the husband delegates the authority to divorce to the wife at the time of marriage. Through this lesson, we will analyse the permissibility, conditions, and practical application of this hilah, and understand why the exact wording is critical.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem and the proposed solution
The passage describes the difficulties women face (oppression, missing husband, impotence, insanity) and proposes writing conditions in the marriage contract to give the wife authority to divorce herself when needed.
The problem is the absence of a Shari'ah judge.
2
Understand the ruling: permissibility
The answer states that such a marriage contract (cabinama) is ja'iz (permissible) and that this delegation is called tafwid al-talaq in fiqh terminology.
3
Note the conditions for validity
The author emphasizes that the exact wording must be used without alteration; otherwise, the affidavit becomes completely useless. The timing (before marriage) is implied.
This is the most critical condition.
4
Recognize the authority and scope
This fatwa is from the later Hanafi tradition (Fatawa Mutakhkhirin) and is a practical solution for dire situations, not a general license for all marriages.
It is based on necessity and the principle of conditions in contracts.

Summary: "Al-Hilat al-Najizah li al-Halilah al-Ajizah" has two parts. First part: delegation of divorce at the time of marriage, i.e., the ruling of the wife effecting divorce herself. Question: Nowadays in India, due to the absence of a Shari'ah judge, the difficulties women face need no explanation. Sometimes the husband oppresses and does not fulfill the wife's rights, neither provides maintenance nor gives divorce. Sometimes the wife abandons children and goes missing. Sometimes the husband is not suitable for the wife, or is impotent, or is insane. If a Shari'ah judge were present, the solution to these difficulties would be easy, but now the extraordinary difficulties are apparent. For this reason, the question is: (1) The remedy prescribed in some places for these difficulties is that at the time of marriage, conditions are written in the marriage contract such that women obtain automatic authority to effect divorce upon themselves when needed. Is this method correct and valid or not? (2) And is there any difference between writing this marriage contract before marriage, after marriage, or exactly at the time of marriage, or having these conditions stated orally? Answer: (1) Writing such a marriage contract in which the authority of divorce is given into the hand of the woman and using it when needed is permissible. In the terminology of fiqh, giving this authority is called tafwid al-talaq, i.e., entrusting the right of divorce to the woman. (2) There are numerous forms of this tafwid al-talaq, the details of which along with conditions are mentioned in the original treatise "Al-Hilat al-Najizah". Here only two forms are described which are easiest for the common people, most beneficial for women, and include all kinds of expediency for both parties. And that is: before marriage, a written affidavit containing the following words should be obtained from the husband. It should be clear that every word of this affidavit has been written after careful consideration in accordance with Shari'ah rules, with full regard for the interests of both parties. None of these words should be changed; otherwise, in some cases this affidavit will become completely useless and fruitless. And that affidavit in the form of a marriage contract is as follows:

Commentary
This passage is a legal stratagem (hila) case from the Hanafi work Al-Hilat al-Najizah. It begins by identifying the first part of the book: delegation of divorce (tafwid al-talaq) at the time of marriage. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, highlights the practical problem: in contemporary India, the absence of a qualified Shari'ah judge leaves women trapped in difficult marriages (oppression, non-maintenance, missing husbands, impotence, insanity). The proposed solution is to include conditions in the marriage contract that give the wife the authority to divorce herself when needed. The answer clearly states that such a condition is permissible (ja'iz) and that giving this authority is termed 'tafwid al-talaq'. The author then notes that there are multiple forms of tafwid, and he will present two that are easy and beneficial. He emphasizes that the exact wording provided must be used without alteration; changing any word could render the affidavit useless. This is a critical condition for the validity of the hila. The passage ends with the beginning of the sample affidavit template. The ruling here establishes the permissibility of this hila based on the principle of necessity and the general permissibility of conditions in marriage contracts, as long as they do not contradict Shari'ah.

Key Terms
تفویض طلاق (tafwid al-talaq): The act of the husband delegating the authority to divorce to the wife, usually at the time of marriage, so that she can divorce herself upon the occurrence of specified conditions.
حیلہ ناجزہ (al-hilat al-najizah): A successful/effective legal stratagem; specifically the title of Thanwi's work containing permissible solutions for women's marital problems.

Hila for Delegated Divorce via Conditional Contract (Tafwid al-Talaq)
Explaining a hila for delegated divorce via conditional contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a valid tafwid al-talaq clause in a marriage contract and identify the conditions that make it operative under Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Tafwid al-talaq gives the wife authority to divorce herself upon breach of specific conditions — a valid hila that must follow precise wording.

This lesson unpacks a practical hila used to protect women's rights by delegating divorce authority. The sample contract (kabin nama) is carefully worded to comply with Shari'ah and must not be altered. Understanding the conditions and limits of this delegation is critical for a mufti advising on family law matters.

Guided Path
1
State the hila's purpose
Identify that this hila enables a wife to divorce herself (talaq ba'in) when the husband violates specific conditions, protecting her from harm.
The purpose is a beneficial legal stratagem within Shari'ah boundaries.
2
Define tafwid al-talaq
Recognize tafwid al-talaq as the husband delegating his right to divorce to the wife, making her the agent for a conditional self-divorce.
Hanafi fiqh permits this delegation under certain conditions.
3
List conditions for validity
Extract from the source: (1) Clear specification of conditions, (2) Two witnesses confirm breach, (3) Wife's authority is for one month per violation, (4) Authority lapses after month but renews with new breach, (5) Authority is limited to that marriage only.
The contract wording is fixed; any change may void the hila.
4
Explain the mechanism
Trace: Husband violates condition → two witnesses confirm → wife gets one month to pronounce one talaq ba'in → if not used, authority expires → new violation restarts the one-month window.
This mechanism renews per violation but does not accumulate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجواب

اقرار نامہ لکھتا ہوں تاکہ میں اس کا پابند رہوں، اور پابندی نہ ہونے کی صورت میں سمات مذکور کے لیے رہائی کی صورت ہو سکے ۔
پیس میں اقرار کرتا ہوں کہ جب تک وہ میرے نکاح میں رہے ، میں مندرجہ ذیل شرائط کا پابند رہوں گا ، اور مسماۃ کے اطمینان کے لیے لکھتا ہوں کہ اگر میں مسماۃ مذکورہ سے نکاح کروں تو نکاح کرنے کے بعد جب کبھی اس کو اس نکاح ہیں یہ لکھتے ہوئے مندرجہ ذیل اشخاص میں سے کم از کم دو حضرات تسلیم کر لیں تو اس کے بعد سماہ مذکورہ کواختیار ہوگا کہ اسی وقت یا خلاف شرط تسلیم ہونے سے ایک ہینہ تک پھر کسی وقت چاہے خود پر ایک طلاق بائن واقع کر کے اس نکاح سے علیحدہ ہو جائے اور جب کبھی کسی شرط کا خلاف واقع ہو ہر ایک مرتبہ ایک ایک ماہ کے لیے اختیار حاصل ہوتا رہے گا، لیکن یہ اختیار ایک ہی نکاح تک محدود ہے اگر کسی طریقہ سے علیحدگی کے بعد نکاح کا اعادہ ہو تو اس کے بعد یہ اختیار اور شرائط نہیں بلکہ اس وقت جو کچھ دوبارہ طے ہو جائے اس کے موافق عمل ہوگا۔ ان آدمیوں

The answer: 55. This type of marriage contract writing in which the authority of divorce is placed in the wife's hand, and using it at the time of need is permissible. In juristic terminology, this giving of authority is called 'tafwid al-talaq' i.e., entrusting the right of divorce to the woman. (2) There are multiple forms of this tafwid al-talaq, whose detail with conditions is mentioned in the original treatise 'Al-Hilat al-Najizah'. Here only two forms are explained, which are the easiest for the common people, most beneficial for women, and comprehensive of all kinds of interest for both parties. And that is: before marriage, a declaration should be written from the husband with the following words. It should be noted that every word of this declaration has been written after deliberation, in accordance with Islamic legal principles, fully observing the interests of both parties. None of these words should be changed; otherwise in some cases this declaration will become completely useless and futile. And that declaration in the form of a marriage contract is as follows: Date--- [The template continues with names, conditions, etc.] [Page 55] ... I declare that as long as she remains in my marriage, I will be bound by the following conditions, and for the satisfaction of the named woman I write: if I marry the aforementioned woman, then after marriage, whenever at least two of the following persons confirm that I have violated a condition, then after that the named woman will have the authority that at that very time or within one month from the confirmation of violation, at any time she wishes, she may effect one irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) upon herself and separate from this marriage. And whenever any condition is violated, each time she will get authority for one month. But this authority is limited to this marriage only; if after separation the marriage is renewed, then this authority and conditions are not applicable; rather whatever is agreed anew at that time will be acted upon. [Names of witnesses] ... After writing the above marriage contract, upon one violation of a condition, the woman will get authority only for one month, and at the end of the month the authority lapses. But thereafter if any condition is violated again, then again she gets authority for one month. And the mahr (dower) once violated? from this method the authority...
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage presents a hila (legal stratagem) from Hanafi fiqh to enable a woman to divorce herself if the husband violates certain conditions. The stratagem is based on the concept of tafwid al-talaq, where the husband delegates the right of divorce to the wife. The sample contract (kabin nama) must be written exactly as given, as altering any word may invalidate the hila. The conditions include: the husband agrees to specific terms (not detailed here but implicit), and if two witnesses confirm his violation, the wife gets the authority to pronounce one talaq ba'in upon herself within one month. This authority renews each time a violation occurs, but only for that particular marriage. If remarriage occurs, new terms must be agreed. This hila is designed to be practical and beneficial, especially for women, while adhering to Shari'ah rules. The author emphasizes that the wording is carefully crafted and must not be changed.

Key Terms
تفویض طلاق (tafwid al-talaq): Delegation of the right to divorce by the husband to the wife, giving her authority to divorce herself under specified conditions.
کابین نامہ (kabin nama): A marriage contract document that records the terms of marriage, including mahr and special conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if the husband violates a condition but no witnesses confirm within the one-month window?
A) The wife's authority remains indefinitely until she uses it.
B) The wife's authority lapses at the end of the month even without use.
C) The violation is automatically considered forgiven.
D) The wife must renew the contract.

Key Takeaway
The hila of tafwid al-talaq is valid in Hanafi fiqh but requires strict adherence to precise wording and conditions to be effective.

Conditional Delegation of Divorce (Tafwid al-Talaq) Deed
Sample deed for conditional talaq delegation (hila)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze a conditional talaq delegation deed (hila) by identifying its key clauses, conditions, and legal effects according to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A conditional delegation deed grants the wife a limited, time-bound option to divorce herself upon breach of stipulations, but only within the current marriage.

This lesson presents a sample deed (iqrarnama) used for conditional delegation of divorce (tafwid al-talaq), a Hanafi legal stratagem (hila). It allows the husband to empower his wife to divorce herself if he fails to fulfill certain conditions. Understanding the precise wording and legal effects is essential for muftis advising on such arrangements. We will parse the deed's clauses and examine the conditions that govern the wife's option.

Guided Path
1
Identify Key Legal Terms
Locate the terms tafwid al-talaq (delegation of divorce), talaq ba'in (irrevocable divorce), ikhtiyar (option), and shart (condition) in the deed. Define each in Hanafi legal context.
These terms define the nature and limitations of the wife's right.
2
Determine Parties and Roles
The husband is the undertaking party (muqirr), the wife is the beneficiary (musamma), and two witnesses are required for confirmation of breach. Identify their legal capacities.
Witnesses act as verifiers of condition breach, not as judges.
3
Analyze Trigger Mechanism
The wife's option activates when two witnesses confirm a breach of a condition. Note the condition must be specified (e.g., not remarrying certain individuals, paying maintenance).
The confirmation must be in writing according to the deed.
4
Examine Scope and Limitations
The option lasts one month from confirmation of breach. It lapses after that month but renews upon each new breach. The option is limited to the current marriage; if remarriage occurs, the deed is void and a new agreement is needed.
Each breach grants a separate one-month window; multiple breaches cannot be accumulated.
5
Evaluate Legal Effects
If the wife exercises her option, she issues one talaq ba'in, ending the marriage. The husband cannot revoke this divorce. If she does not exercise within the month, the option lapses without effect.
The deed stipulates only one ba'in divorce per breach, not multiple.

Source Text

گواہ میرا
گواہ نمبر ۲
I write this deed of undertaking so that I remain bound by it, and in case of non-compliance, there may be a way of release for the aforementioned woman. I hereby undertake that as long as she remains in my marriage, I will be bound by the following conditions, and for the satisfaction of the named woman, I write that if I contract marriage with the aforementioned woman, after contracting marriage, whenever two of the following persons at least confirm this in writing, then the aforementioned woman will have the option to immediately or within one month from the confirmation of breach of condition, at any time, if she wishes, to effect one ba'in divorce upon herself and separate from this marriage; and whenever any condition is violated, each time she will receive the option for one month. But this option is limited to one marriage; if after separation there is a remarriage, then this option and conditions are not applicable; rather, whatever is agreed upon anew at that time will be acted upon. The names of these persons are: Name, Conditions are: Name. Violation of the condition of this deed: after writing the above marriage deed, upon one violation of a condition, the woman will receive the option for only one month, and at the end of the month the option will lapse. But thereafter if there is another violation of any condition, then again she will receive the option for one month, and in this manner option will continue to be granted upon each violation. However, if the woman effectuates divorce once or separation occurs in any other way, then upon remarriage, no option will arise from violation of conditions. I have accepted this deed. ---- Signature. Witness 1, Witness 2.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage presents a sample deed (iqrarnama) for conditional delegation of divorce (tafwid al-talaq), a legal stratagem (hila) in the Hanafi school. It allows a husband to grant his wife the right to divorce herself if he breaches specified conditions. The deed outlines the mechanics: the wife's option becomes active upon confirmation by two witnesses that a condition was violated. The option is limited to one ba'in divorce per violation, and it must be exercised within one month of the violation; after the month, the option lapses but is renewed upon each subsequent violation. Importantly, the option is tied to the current marriage contract; if separation occurs (by divorce or other means) and the couple remarries, the original delegation is nullified, and a new agreement would be required. This demonstrates the Hanafi legal principle of tawkil (delegation) in talaq and the importance of conditional stipulations to protect the wife's rights. The deed also includes space for witness names, emphasizing the requirement of testimony for legal effect.

Key Terms
تفویض طلاق (tafwid al-talaq): Delegation of the right to divorce to the wife or a third party.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): A final, irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage and requires a new contract to remarry.
اختیار (ikhtiyar): The option granted to the wife to divorce herself upon condition breach.
شرط (shart): Condition that the husband must fulfill; breach triggers the wife's option.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One month
B) One year
C) Until remarriage
D) Indefinitely

Key Takeaway
The conditional delegation deed is a valid Hanafi hila that gives the wife a limited, renewable option to divorce herself upon breach of conditions, but it is tied to the current marriage contract.

Conditions for Adopting Another Madhhab in Severe Necessity
Defines conditions for adopting another madhhab with necessity and scholarly verification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a Hanafi mufti may adopt a ruling from another madhhab and identify what constitutes valid necessity.

Core Idea
Adopting another madhhab requires severe necessity recognized by scholars, not personal whim.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on adopting rulings from other madhhabs. While the school generally prohibits talfiq (mixing rulings), it permits qualified scholars to give fatwa based on another imam's madhhab when severe necessity arises. However, strict conditions must be met to prevent abuse. We will explore these conditions, especially the definition of valid necessity and the role of scholarly verification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being discussed? The act of a mufti giving fatwa according to a non-Hanafi madhhab. The ruling is ja'iz (permissible) under conditions.
Not permissible for laypeople to do on their own.
2
List the conditions
From the text, extract the conditions: (1) severe necessity (darurat shadida), (2) general affliction (umum balwa), (3) not due to whimsical desire, (4) recognized by insightful scholars (ulama ahl basirat)
The first part of the text mentions 'shurūṭ wa quyūdāt' generally.
3
Define darurat (necessity)
Analyze the term darurat as used here. It is defined as a severe hardship that relaxes normal prohibitions. The text specifies that it must be recognized by scholars of insight, not merely personal opinion.
Refer to legal_definition_dissector for darurat.
4
Understand the role of scholarly verification
The text emphasizes that multiple verifying scholars must acknowledge the necessity before adopting another madhhab. This prevents individual caprice.
The author cites the collective endorsement of Deoband scholars.
5
Apply the qawida 'al-mashaqqa tujlib al-taysir'
The permissibility is based on the major maxim that hardship brings ease. Recognize that this qawida justifies the ruling but is restricted by the conditions.
Qawida block provided.

نے اس کتاب کی روایت میں وضاحت فرمائی ہے۔
شدید ضرورت اور عموم بلوی کے وقت شدید ضرورت کے وقت کی گنجائش حنفیہ کے نزدیک دوسرے ائمہ کے مذہب کو (مع شرائط و قیودات) اختیار کر کے اس پر فتوی دینا بھی جائز ہے لیکن عوام کو خود اپنی راستے سے جس مسئلہ میں چاہیں ایسا کر لینے کی اجازت نہیں بلکہ بڑی احتیاط کی ضرورت ہے ۔ " وذالك لما صرح به العلامة الشافعي رسالة شرح المنظومة فى رسم المفتى وقد مر نصه في تمهيد هند و الرسالة.
اپنا مذہب نہ چھوڑنے کی تاکید اس زمانہ میں احتیاط اس طریقہ سے ہوسکتی ہے کہ جب تک محقق و متدین علماء کرام میں سے متعدد حضرات کسی مسئلہ میں ضرور کا پایا جانا تسلیم کر کے دوسرے امام کے مذہب پر لے وہ روایت یہ ہے داما المتعنت المتمنع عن الانفاق ..... فلها القيام فان لم ثبت عسرة انفق الطلق والاطلق عليه قال محشيه قوله والاطلق عليه الحاكم من غير تلوم الى ان قل وان تطوع بالنفقة قريب لو اجنبي فقال ابن القاسم لها التفارق لان الفراق قد وجب لها وقال عبد الرحمن لا مقال لها لان سبب الفراق هو عدم النفقه قد انفى وهو الذي تقضيه المدوله الم (ناقل خورشید حسن قاسمی) حیلہ ناجزہ اورا کا برین ہند : اس وجہ سے ہم نے اس رسالہ میں چند مسائل مذہب مالکیہ سے لینے کی ضرورت سمجھی تو صرف اپنی رائے پر قناعت نہیں کی بلکہ مسودہ مرتب کر کے حضرات علماء دیوبند سہارن پور کی خدمت میں رائے لینے کے لیے پیش کیا گیا اُن حضرات نے جس اہتمام کے ساتھ جمع ہو کر اس پر نظر فرمائی ہے ایسا اتفاق شاید ہی کسی مسئلہ میں پیش آیا ہو یہاں تک کہ اس اہم کام کی وجہ سے ان حضرات نے چند مرتبہ اپنی مشغولیات کا غیر معمولی خرچ بھی کیا اور بالآخر متعدد مرتبہ باہمی مشورہ کے بعد تمام حضرات نے متفقہ طور پر تصدیق فرمائی۔ اس کے بعد شائع ہوا۔
فتوی نہ دیں، اُس وقت تک ہر گزا اپنے امام کے مذہب کو نہ چھوڑے کیونکہ مذہب غیر کو لیتے ریعنی دوسرے امام کے مذہب پر عمل کرنے کے لیے یہ شرط ہے کہ ایسا کرنا شہوت نفسانی کی وجہ سے نہ ہو بلکہ ضرورت شدیدہ کی وجہ سے ہو اور ضرورت وہ ہی معتبر ہے جس کو علماء اہل بصیرت ضرورت سمجھیں نیز یہ بھی ضروری ہے کہ فتوی دینے والا ایسا شخص ہو کہ جس نے کسی ماہر استاذ سے فن کو حاصل کیا ہو اور حضرات اہل بصیرت اس کو فقہ میں مہارت تامہ حاصل ہونے پر شہادت دیتے ہوں ۔ " لما قال الشامي في عقود اسم المفتى فان المتقدمين شرطه افي المفتى الاجتهاد وهذا مفقود في زماننا فلا اقل من ان يشترط فيه معرفة المسائل بشروطها وقيود التي كثيرا ما يسقطونها والا يصرحون بها اعتماد على فهو المتفقه وكذا الابر من معرفت عرف زمانه واحوالى اهله والتحزيم في ذالك على استاذ ماهر الخير شامی
مذکورہ بالا عبارت کا مفہوم یہ ہے کہ متقدمین مجے مفتی کے لیے شرائط ر کے مذہب پر فائز ہونے) کے لیے اجتہاد کی شرط لگائی ہے اور یہ شرط اس زمانہ میں مفقود ہے پس کم از کم اس میں یہ شرط ضرور رہے گی کہ مسائل سے ان کی شرائط و قیودات کے ساتھ واقف ہو لینی)
لے ایک بات یہ بھی پیش نظر رہنا چاہیے۔ اگر کسی جگہ مسلک مالکیہ کے قاضی نہ ہوں، یا جس جگہ بالکل قاضی ہی نہ ہوں اگر وہاں پر مالکہ کے مذہب کی پنچائیت ہو تو خفی ، قاضی اور حنفی پنچائیت کی طرف رجوع بند کیا جائے۔ اور اگر کوئی رجوع کرے تو ان کو مالکی مذہب پر فیصلہ کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ، بلکہ مالکی قاضی یا مالکی پنچائیت میں معامل پیش کیا جائے ۔
He explained the narration of this book. In severe necessity and general affliction, according to the Hanafis, it is also permissible to adopt the madhhab of other imams (with conditions and restrictions) and give fatwa upon it. But the common people are not allowed to do so on their own in any issue they wish; rather, great caution is required. And that is because al-Allamah al-Shafi'i [sic] stated in the treatise Sharh al-Manzumah fi Rasm al-Mufti, and its text has already passed in the introduction to Hind wa al-Risalah. The insistence on not leaving one's own madhhab in this time can be precautionary in this way: until multiple scholars from the verifying and religious scholars acknowledge that necessity has been established in a matter, then one may adopt the madhhab of another imam. That narration is: 'As for the obstinate one who refrains from spending... she may seek recourse. If hardship is not established, he spends and the divorce is issued and the judge pronounces it without delay until it becomes little. And if a stranger voluntarily assumes the maintenance, Ibn al-Qasim said: she may separate because separation has become obligatory for her. And Abd al-Rahman said: she has no say because the cause of separation, which is lack of maintenance, has been removed. And this is what the Mudawwanah supports.' (Transmitted by Khurshid Hasan Qasimi) Hila Najizah wa Ila... Barain Hind. For this reason, in this treatise we considered the need to take several issues from the Maliki madhhab, so we did not content ourselves with our own opinion; rather, we prepared a draft and presented it to the scholars of Deoband and Saharanpur for their opinion. Those scholars gathered and reviewed it with such care that such agreement has hardly occurred in any issue. They even made extraordinary sacrifices of their time several times due to this important work, and finally after multiple consultations, all scholars unanimously endorsed it. Afterward it was published. Do not give a fatwa; until then, one should never leave the madhhab of his imam, because adopting a non-madhhab, i.e., acting upon the madhhab of another imam, has the condition that it should not be due to whimsical desire but due to severe necessity. And necessity is considered only when scholars of insight deem it necessity. Also, it is necessary that the one giving fatwa be a person who has acquired the science from an expert teacher, and the insightful scholars bear witness that he has complete expertise in fiqh. As al-Shami said in 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: 'The early scholars conditioned ijtihad in the mufti, which is lacking in our time, so at the very least it should be conditioned that he knows the masail with their conditions and restrictions, which they often omit or do not mention explicitly, relying on understanding. Similarly, it is necessary to know the custom of his time and the conditions of its people, and to be trained in that by an expert teacher.' The meaning of the above expression is that the early scholars laid down the condition of ijtihad for the mufti (to be qualified to give fatwa on another madhhab), and this condition is absent in this time, so at minimum this condition remains: that he be acquainted with the masail along with their conditions and restrictions. Also, one point should be kept in mind: If in a place there are no Maliki judges, or in a place there are no judges at all, but there is a Maliki panchayat, then one should refer to a Maliki judge or a Hanafi panchayat. And if someone refers to them, they do not need to decide according to the Maliki madhhab; rather, the case should be presented before a Maliki judge or Maliki panchayat.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the treatise's discussion on the permissibility of adopting rulings from another madhhab (specifically the Maliki madhhab) in cases of severe necessity. The author first affirms that, according to the Hanafi school, it is permissible for a qualified scholar to give a fatwa based on another imam's ruling when there is severe necessity and general affliction, provided that all conditions and restrictions are observed. However, laypeople are absolutely forbidden from picking and choosing rulings according to their whims; this is a matter requiring great caution. The author then quotes from a work on Rasm al-Mufti (the science of issuing fatwas) to emphasize that one should not abandon one's own madhhab lightly. Instead, multiple verifying scholars must acknowledge that necessity exists before adopting another madhhab. A lengthy Arabic quote from Maliki jurisprudence is provided as an example of the type of rulings that might be adopted—specifically concerning maintenance and divorce. The author then explains that the present treatise contains several issues taken from the Maliki madhhab, and the process of scholarly verification involved multiple senior scholars from Deoband and Saharanpur who collectively endorsed the work. The passage reiterates the key conditions for following another madhhab: (1) it must be due to severe necessity, not personal desire, (2) the necessity must be recognized by insightful scholars, and (3) the mufti must be fully qualified—having studied under an expert teacher and having been recognized by scholars as having complete mastery of fiqh. The passage also cites Ibn Abidin (al-Shami) from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, stating that since ijtihad is lacking in later times, the minimum requirement for a mufti is knowledge of the masail with their conditions and restrictions, awareness of custom and circumstances, and training under a master. Finally, practical guidance is given: if a Maliki judge is available, cases should be referred to him; otherwise, a Hanafi judge or panchayat should follow the Maliki ruling when necessary.

Key Terms
مذهب غير (madhhab ghayr): The madhhab of another imam (other than one's own) adopted for a specific ruling in necessity.
شرائط و قيودات (shurūṭ wa quyūdāt): Conditions and restrictions that must be observed when adopting a ruling from another madhhab.
ضرورت (ḍarūrat): A severe necessity that justifies departing from one's usual madhhab; must be recognized by insightful scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary condition for a Hanafi mufti to give fatwa based on another madhhab?
A) The ruling must be from the Maliki madhhab.
B) There must be severe necessity recognized by insightful scholars.
C) The mufti must have personal ijtihad.
D) The ruling must be easier than the Hanafi ruling.

Key Takeaway
Adopting another madhhab is permissible only when severe necessity is established and verified by multiple qualified scholars, not by personal desire.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate
8 min
Qualifications of the Mufti and Practical Guidance on Referral
Defines mufti qualifications and referral rules for mixed schools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the minimum qualifications required for a mufti to give fatwa on another madhhab and apply the rule of referral to appropriate authorities in mixed-madhhab situations.

Core Idea
A mufti must be trained under an expert, know conditions of masail, and be recognized by scholars; laypeople cannot switch madhhabs.

This lesson focuses on the personal qualifications a mufti must have to legitimately adopt a non-Hanafi ruling. Building on the earlier conditions, the passage makes clear that even when necessity exists, the mufti must be fully competent. It also provides practical guidance on referring cases to Maliki judges or panchayats. Understanding these qualifications prevents unqualified individuals from issuing fatwas that could mislead the community.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mufti's required qualifications
From the text, list: (1) studied fiqh under an expert teacher (ustadh mahir), (2) recognized as having complete expertise (maharata tamma) by insightful scholars, (3) knowledge of masail with their conditions and restrictions, (4) awareness of custom and conditions of the people.
Ibn Abidin's quote is the source.
2
Understand the rationale for these qualifications
Since ijtihad is lacking in later times, the minimum is that the mufti knows the masail thoroughly and has practical training. This ensures he does not omit conditions or make errors.
The text says 'falan aqallu min an yushturata fihi ma'rifat al-masa'il bi shurutiha wa quyudiha'.
3
Recognize the prohibition for laypeople
The passage reiterates that common people (awam) are not allowed to pick and choose madhhabs. Only qualified muftis can do so under conditions.
This prevents chaos and talfiq.
4
Apply the referral rule
If a case requires a Maliki ruling, it should be referred to a Maliki judge or panchayat if available. A Hanafi judge should not decide according to Maliki law unless necessary.
Practical guidance for mixed-madhhab situations.

لے ایک بات یہ بھی پیش نظر رہنا چاہیے۔ اگر کسی جگہ مسلک مالکیہ کے قاضی نہ ہوں، یا جس جگہ بالکل قاضی ہی نہ ہوں اگر وہاں پر مالکہ کے مذہب کی پنچائیت ہو تو خفی ، قاضی اور حنفی پنچائیت کی طرف رجوع بند کیا جائے۔ اور اگر کوئی رجوع کرے تو ان کو مالکی مذہب پر فیصلہ کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ، بلکہ مالکی قاضی یا مالکی پنچائیت میں معامل پیش کیا جائے ۔

A lengthy Arabic quote from Maliki jurisprudence is provided as an example of the type of rulings that might be adopted—specifically concerning maintenance and divorce. The author then explains that the present treatise contains several issues taken from the Maliki madhhab, and the process of scholarly verification involved multiple senior scholars from Deoband and Saharanpur who collectively endorsed the work. The passage reiterates the key conditions for following another madhhab: (1) it must be due to severe necessity, not personal desire, (2) the necessity must be recognized by insightful scholars, and (3) the mufti must be fully qualified—having studied under an expert teacher and having been recognized by scholars as having complete mastery of fiqh. The passage also cites Ibn Abidin (al-Shami) from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, stating that since ijtihad is lacking in later times, the minimum requirement for a mufti is knowledge of the masail with their conditions and restrictions, awareness of custom and circumstances, and training under a master. Finally, practical guidance is given: if a Maliki judge is available, cases should be referred to him; otherwise, a Hanafi judge or panchayat should follow the Maliki ruling when necessary.

Key Terms
ماهِر استاذ (ustādh māhir): An expert teacher from whom the mufti must have acquired the science of fiqh.
أهل بصيرت (ahl baṣīrat): Insightful scholars who can recognize true necessity and certify the mufti's expertise.
شرائط و قيود المسائل (shurūṭ wa quyūd al-masā'il): The conditions and restrictions attached to each legal ruling; the mufti must know them completely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a Hanafi judge do when a case requires a Maliki ruling and a Maliki judge is available?
A) The Hanafi judge should apply the Maliki ruling himself.
B) The case should be referred to the Maliki judge.
C) The Hanafi judge should refuse to hear the case.
D) The case should be decided according to Hanafi fiqh regardless.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must be formally trained and certified, and in mixed-madhhab cases, refer to the appropriate authority rather than adopting rulings on his own.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems

Condition for Following Another Madhhab: Mansoos Requirement
Explaining the condition that a ruling must be explicitly stated in another madhhab for a valid hila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that a ruling must be mansoos (explicitly stated) in the other madhhab for a valid hila, and apply it to evaluate the validity of a fatwa based on qiyas.

Core Idea
Following another madhhab requires the ruling to be mansoos; analogy without explicit text is invalid.

In this lesson, we examine a key rasm al-mufti principle: when can a mufti depart from his own madhhab and adopt the ruling of another madhhab as a legal stratagem (hila)? The source passage, from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilatul Najijah, clarifies that such adoption is only valid if the ruling is explicitly stated (mansoos) in that madhhab, not derived by analogy (qiyas). The case of taking payment for reciting the Quran at graves serves as a practical illustration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rasm Rule
Locate the statement in the passage that defines when one can give a fatwa by adopting another madhhab. The rule is explicitly that the permissibility must be 'clearly established and explicitly stated' (mansoos) in that madhhab.
The passage contrasts this with deriving permissibility by qiyas on the other madhhab.
2
Examine the Application
Consider the example given: payment for reciting the Quran at graves. The proponents claimed necessity and analogized to payment for teaching (which is mansoos in Maliki and Shafi'i schools). Identify why this analogy fails: the new case (recitation) is not mansoos in those schools.
The author argues that even if necessity were accepted, the ruling must still be mansoos; analogy by non-mujtahids is invalid.
3
Analyze the Concept of Mansoos
Use the legal definition dissector from the toolbox to understand what makes a ruling mansoos: it is explicitly stated by the Imam or transmitted from him, as opposed to derived by qiyas.
The source emphasizes that the ruling must be textually established, not deduced.
4
Understand the Role of 'Illah
The passage discusses Ibn Abideen's phrase 'wa in wajadta fīhi al-hīlah'. The 'illah referred to is the wisdom (hikmah) in the original mansoos issue, not the cause of necessity. This distinction prevents arbitrary extension of a hila.
If necessity were the criterion, Ibn Abideen would have used 'darurah' or 'hajah'.
5
Respond to the Objection of Interpretative Probability
The passage presents two responses to the objection that there are two possible interpretations of Ibn Abideen's phrase. The first: probability harms the one who uses it as evidence; the second: the author's interpretation is necessary to maintain consistency with Ibn Abideen's other positions.
This demonstrates the method of tafsir al-nass by internal consistency.

One can give a fatwa on the permissibility of a thing by adopting the madhhab (of another Imam) only when its permissibility is explicitly established and clearly stated in the madhhab of that other Imam. It is not valid to establish the permissibility of a thing that is not explicitly stated (mansoos) in the other madhhab by analogy (qiyas) on that madhhab, and then give a fatwa on that contrived permissibility due to necessity. As some people in the time of Allama Shanai [Thanwi] claimed necessity and declared taking compensation for recitation of the Quran at graves permissible, and in this matter they analogized to the permissibility of payment for teaching. This explanation (of payment for teaching) is clearly present in the madhhabs of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i. And at this place, Allama's actual purpose is to reject this invalid analogy (qiyas fāsid).

The gist of the above discussion is that the necessity for taking payment for recitation of the Quran is unacceptable, a necessity that would make it permissible to leave one's own madhhab. And even if we accept that necessity, it still cannot be permissible because in no madhhab is its permissibility explicitly stated (mansoos). And teaching, which is mansoos, cannot be analogized to recitation by the people of this time, due to their not being mujtahids, even though conveying reward to the deceased is present in recitation as well, which is the proof of the original issue (ruqya or giving charity) that exists in the noble hadith.

And for this same reason, Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i declared payment for teaching permissible. And because of the same, after the phrase 'khilāf intifā‘ihī' (contrary to its benefit), he said 'wa in wajadta fīhi al-hīlah' (and if you find a legal stratagem in it), meaning even if the effective cause ('illah) of the original mansoos issue in the madhhab is found. Otherwise, if the meaning was what those people thought, then it would have been appropriate to say 'idhā damast ilayhi al-hājah' or 'in idda‘at ilayhi al-darūrah' etc., because the necessity of analogy (qiyas) of one issue upon another is in the 'illah.

The summary of this second answer is that in the translation of the phrase 'wa in wajadta fīhi al-hīlah', the word 'al-hīlah' refers to the effective cause that is the wisdom in the original mansoos issue in the madhhab, not the cause of necessity, which caused those people difficulty.

Now the remaining question: in this passage related to acting upon another madhhab, when both probabilities exist, how can one be determined? The first answer is that probability harms the one who uses it as evidence. Since we do not use this passage as evidence, even if the second probability remains, it does not harm us. Rather, those who use it as evidence are the people who limit taking the ruling of another madhhab to a specific time. For us, it is sufficient to extract such a probability by which the passage is used, and to prove that it has only this one meaning.

The second answer regarding the connection with the other madhhab is that what we have expressed is determined, because without it, the statement of Allama Ibn Abidin (Shami) cannot be correct. For Allama himself, in his treatise 'Shifa' al-'Alil' and also in Radd al-Muhtar (Fatawa Shami), accepted the permissibility of employing for teaching fiqh, imamat, adhan, and wa'z, even though...
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of a hila (legal stratagem) case: taking payment for reciting the Quran at graves. The central issue is the conditions under which one may follow another madhhab to permit something otherwise impermissible in one's own madhhab. The author (Ashraf Ali Thanwi) states a rasm rule: following another madhhab for a fatwa is only valid if the permissibility of the act is explicitly stated (mansoos) in that madhhab, not deduced by qiyas (analogy). He criticizes contemporaries who, claiming necessity, analogized payment for recitation to payment for teaching (which is mansoos in Maliki and Shafi'i schools). Their fallacy is that they performed qiyas without being mujtahids and applied it to a case that is not mansoos in any madhhab. Thanwi then interprets Ibn Abideen's phrase 'wa in wajadta fīhi al-hīlah' from Radd al-Muhtar. He explains that the 'illah mentioned is the wisdom (hikmah) in the original mansoos issue (teaching), not the necessity of the new case. If necessity were the criterion, Ibn Abideen would have used terms like 'darurah'. Finally, Thanwi addresses a methodological objection: how to determine which of two interpretative probabilities is correct. He gives two responses: (1) probability harms the one who uses it as evidence; since we do not rely on this passage for our position, we only need to show it can be interpreted consistently; (2) his interpretation is the only one that makes Ibn Abideen's broader positions consistent, as Ibn Abideen permitted payment for teaching duties but not for recitation per se.

Key Terms
منصوص (mansoos): حكم ثابت صراحة بقول الإمام أو نقل صحيح عنه
قیاس فاسد (qiyas fāsid): تشبيه حكم بحكم آخر بعلة غير صحيحة أو دون أهلية
علة الحکمة ('illat al-hikmah): السبب الذي هو المناط الحقيقي للحكم الأصلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is a necessary condition for following another madhhab in a hila?
A) The ruling must be derived by qiyas from a similar issue in that madhhab.
B) The ruling must be explicitly stated (mansoos) in that madhhab.
C) The need must be urgent enough to be considered darurah.
D) The person must be a mujtahid at least in that madhhab.

Key Takeaway
A valid hila through adopting another madhhab requires the ruling to be mansoos; analogy alone is insufficient.
