Maliki-based Hila for the Wife of a Missing Husband
Explains Maliki-based hila for mafqud's wife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the Maliki-based legal stratagem (hila) for the wife of a missing husband, stating its classification as revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) and the consequences of the husband's return during or after the iddah.

Core Idea
The court separation for a missing husband is a revocable divorce, not an annulment.

In the Hanafi school, the wife of a missing husband may be able to seek separation after a waiting period, but the Maliki-based hila offers an alternative ruling. This lesson unpacks that hila, showing how the separation is considered a revocable divorce, giving the husband a chance to return during iddah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal nature of the separation
The court separation (tafriq) for a missing husband is classified as talaq raj'i (revocable divorce), not as an annulment or irrevocable divorce.
2
Determine the iddah
The wife observes the iddah of divorce (three menstruations) instead of the iddah of death (four months and ten days).
3
Consider the husband's return during iddah
If the missing husband returns during the iddah period and makes a revocation (raj'a), the marriage continues validly.
4
Consider the husband's return after iddah or without revocation
If he returns after the iddah, or during the iddah but does not revoke, the divorce becomes irrevocable (talaq ba'in), and the wife is free to remarry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر تفریق رفسخ نکاح اس قانون کے مفقود کی رجعت سے تعلق مسئلہ مطابق کیا جائے تو اس بات کا خیال ضروری ہے کہ یہ تفریق طلاق رجعی ہوگی اور اس صورت میں مفقود کی بیوی کو عدت وفات گزارنے کے بجائے طلاق کی عدت تین حیض گزار نے ہوں گے اور اگر مفقود اس صورت میں واپس آگیا تو اس میں یہ تفصیل ہوگی کہ اگر عدت کے دوران اگر رجعت کرے تو رجعت صحیح ہو جائے گی اور بیوی بدستور اُس کے نکاح میں رہے گی اور اگر عدت کے بعد مفقود آگیا یا پہلے ہی آگیا لیکن عدت کے اندر قولی یا فعلی رجعت نہ کی تو اب مفقود کی بیوی پر طلاق بائنہ ہو کر وہ عورت خود مختار ہو گی خواہ وہ عورت دوبارہ اُسی شخص سے نکاح کرے یا کسی دوسرے شخص سے جیسا کہ علامہ صالح تونسی کی روایت کے [?] میں مذکور ہے ۔ زوجہ مفقود کی مدت انتظار کب سے شمار ہوگی ؟ لیکن یہ بات کہ یہ سال مفقود کے غائب ہونے کے وقت سے شمار کیا جائے گا یا قاضی یا شرعی کمیٹی میں عورت کے مقدمہ دائر کرنے کے وقت سے شمار ہوگا تو فتاوی مالکیہ (جہاں سے پر عمل لیا گیا ہے) میں مذکور نہیں ہے اور مالکی مذہب کی جس قدر کتب یہاں موجود تھیں ان میں بھی نہیں مل سکی، اور ظاہر ہے کہ احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ مقدمہ پیش کرنے سے انتظار کا سال شمار کیا جائے۔ کے قدیم نسخہ میں ہی [?] ضمون حاشیہ پر تھا جس کو بعنوان بالا پیش کیا گیا ہے (خورشید حسن قاسمی)
If the separation (tafriq) is made in accordance with this law regarding the issue of the missing husband's (mafqud) return, then it is necessary to consider that this separation will be a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i). In this case, the wife of the missing husband, instead of observing the iddah of death, will observe the iddah of divorce of three menstruations. And if the missing husband returns in this situation, then there is this detail: if he returns during the iddah period, the return will be valid and the wife will remain in his marriage. And if the missing husband comes after the iddah, or came earlier but did not make a verbal or actual return (raj'a) during the iddah, then the wife of the missing husband will be irrevocably divorced (talaq ba'inah), and she will be free, whether she marries the same person again or someone else, as is mentioned in the narration of Allamah Salih Tunisi. From when will the waiting period of the wife of the missing husband be counted? But the matter of whether this year will be counted from the time of the missing husband's disappearance or from the time the wife files the case in the qadi or the Shariah committee — this is not mentioned in the Maliki fatwa works (from which the practice is taken), nor could it be found in the available books of the Maliki school. And obviously, precaution is that the year of waiting should be counted from the time of filing the case. In the old copy, there was a marginal note which has been presented under the above title. (Khurshid Hasan Qasimi).
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage presents a hila (legal stratagem) derived from the Maliki school for the wife of a missing husband (mafqud). The ruling clarifies that the court's separation (tafriq) is considered a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i). Consequently, the wife observes the iddah of divorce (three menstruations) rather than the iddah of death. If the husband returns during the iddah, he may validly revoke the divorce and resume the marriage. If he returns after the iddah or fails to revoke during it, the divorce becomes irrevocable (talaq ba'inah), freeing the wife to remarry. The timeframe for the waiting period (sana intizar) is an unresolved point in the Maliki sources consulted; the author recommends counting from the date the wife files her case with the qadi or shariah committee, as a matter of caution (ihtiyat). The note at the end indicates this ruling was found in a marginal annotation of an old manuscript.

Key Terms
مفقود (mafqud): A husband who has gone missing and is not known to be alive or dead.
طلاق رجعی (talaq raj'i): Revocable divorce allowing husband to resume marriage without new contract during iddah.
عدت (iddah): Waiting period after divorce or death before remarriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Maliki hila classifies court separation as revocable divorce, giving the missing husband a chance to return during iddah.

Unresolved Issue: When Does the Waiting Year Begin?
Explains unresolved start of waiting year.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the unresolved issue regarding the start of the waiting period for the wife of a missing husband and apply the principle of ihtiyat to determine the operative ruling.

Core Idea
When the source texts are silent, precaution determines the mufta bihi.

The Maliki sources consulted for this hila left one detail ambiguous: when does the one-year waiting period begin? The author recommends starting from the date the wife files the case, as a matter of caution. This lesson examines that ruling.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the lacuna in the Maliki sources
The Maliki fatwa works and available books do not specify whether the waiting year is counted from the husband's disappearance or from the wife's filing of the case.
2
Apply the principle of ihtiyat (caution)
When evidence is unclear, choose the option that safeguards the wife's interests and avoids potential harm. Here, starting from the filing date gives a clearer, more manageable timeline.
3
Adopt the operative ruling
The author recommends counting the waiting year from the date the wife presents her case to the qadi or shariah committee. This becomes the mufta bihi for practical application.

The Wife of a Muta'annit Husband: A Maliki-Based Hila
Question-answer defining a Maliki hila for a wife's separation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a wife of a muta'annit husband may obtain a separation via the Maliki-based hila, and apply the first step of making the husband fear (dal').

Core Idea
Before seeking separation, the wife must first try to make the husband fear — a condition precedent from Maliki fiqh adopted for necessity.

This lesson addresses a pressing modern issue: a husband who can provide nafaqah but deliberately withholds it. In Hanafi law, the wife may sue but cannot automatically separate. However, in times of severe necessity, a hila from the Maliki school is available, which requires the wife to first attempt to warn and deter the husband. This passage defines 'muta'annit' and outlines the initial step before a qadi can order tafriq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms
Pinpoint the term 'muta'annit' (husband withholding nafaqah despite ability) and 'tafriq' (court-ordered separation). Recognize that this hila is borrowed from the Maliki school.
The passage explicitly defines 'muta'annit' in the question.
2
Extract the condition precedent
The answer states that the wife must first try to make the husband fear (ضلع وغیرہ کرے). This is a mandatory first step, not optional.
The Arabic phrase 'ضلع وغیرہ' implies warning or reprimand.
3
Understand the Maliki adoption
The Hanafi school does not grant tafriq for nafaqah alone. The ruling is taken from Maliki fiqh under the principle of darurah (severe necessity).
This represents talfiq (cross-madhhab borrowing) for relief.
4
Apply to a real scenario
Given a wife whose capable husband refuses nafaqah, list the steps: 1) Attempt dal' (warning/mediation). 2) If unlikely to succeed despite best efforts, 3) Present the case to a qadi who can apply the Maliki ruling for tafriq.
The text cuts off but the initial condition is clear.

The Recalcitrant Husband (Muta'annit) and Judicial Separation via Maliki Adoption
Legal case: hila permitting Maliki-based tafriq for non-providing husband

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a fatwa permitting tafriq (judicial separation) for a wife of a muta'annit by applying the Maliki school under the two conditions of extreme necessity, citing the Hanafi rasm al-mufti principle of darurah.

Core Idea
A wife may separate from a non-providing husband only in dire necessity, by adopting the Maliki school.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilatun Najijah deals with a pressing modern problem: the husband who can but will not maintain his wife. While the Hanafi school generally does not permit separation for non-maintenance, Thanwi provides a hila (legal device) by adopting the Maliki position in cases of extreme necessity. In this lesson, you will learn the definition of muta'annit, the two types of necessity that justify the exception, and the proper procedure for obtaining tafriq. This is a classic example of cross-madhhab borrowing in the fatwa tradition.

Guided Path
1
Define and identify the muta'annit
The muta'annit is a husband who has the financial ability but refuses to provide nafaqah (maintenance) and other rights. Thanwi defines him as 'قدرت کے باوجود بیوی کے حقوق نان و نفقہ وغیرہ ادا نہ کرے'.
This is not a poor husband; he is capable and willfully neglectful.
2
State the default Hanafi position
In the Hanafi school, non-payment of maintenance is a debt, not a ground for faskh (annulment). The wife can sue for maintenance but cannot force separation.
The marriage contract is binding; non-payment is a debt.
3
Recognize the exception: adopting Maliki school under darurah
The source states that at times of severe necessity (sakht majburi), the wife may act according to the Maliki school, which allows tafriq for non-maintenance. This is a concession (rukhsah) under the principle that necessity permits departure from the preferred school.
This is not a change in Hanafi fiqh; it is a fatwa practice of legitimate school-switching.
4
Identify the two conditions of extreme necessity
Thanwi lists two: (1) absolute inability to arrange expenses — no one provides and she cannot earn without compromising modesty. (2) ability to arrange maintenance but strong fear of falling into sin by living apart from the husband (e.g., temptation to zina). Either condition suffices.
The second condition shows that even if she can survive, the risk of sin makes the situation dire.
5
Follow the procedural steps for tafriq
The wife must first try to resolve with the husband. If that fails, she takes the case to a qadi or Muslim authority (or a sharia committee). The authority investigates, and if the claim is proven, gives the husband an ultimatum: fulfill rights or divorce, else separation is effected. After separation, if the husband reforms, the wife may return only during 'iddah; after 'iddah, she can remarry him only with a new nikah.
This ensures separation is judicially sanctioned, not unilateral.

Source Text

سخت مجبوری کی حالت میں مذہب مالکیہ پر عمل کرنے کی گنجائش ہے کیوبیکران کے نزدیک متعنت کی بیوی کو تفریق کا حق مل سکتا ہے اور سخت مجبوری کی
دو صورتیں ہیں۔

ایک یہ کہ عورت کے خرچ کا کوئی انتظام نہ ہو سکے یعنی نہ کوئی شخص صورت کے خرچ نان و نفقہ کا انتظام کرتا ہونہ خود خورت عصمت و عزت کی حفاظت کرتے ہوئے آمدنی پر قدرت رکھتی ہو ۔
اور دوسر کی صورت مجبوری کی یہ ہے کہ اگرچہ بہولت یا دشواری سے خرچہ نان و نفقہ کا انتظام ہو سکتا ہے لیکن شوہر سے الگ رہنے میں گناہ ہیں
مبتلا ہونے کا قوی اندیشہ ہو۔ اور تفریق کی صورت یہ ہے کہ عورت اپنا مقدمہ قاضی شرع یا مسلمان ، اور ان دونوں کے نہ ہونے کی صورت میں (شرعی کمیٹی جماعت مسلمین میں پیش کرے اور جس شخص کے پاس پیش ہو وہ معاملہ کی شرعی شہادت وغیرہ کے ذریعہ سے مکمل تحقیق کرے اور اگر عورت کا دعویٰ صحیح ثابت ہو کہ وسعت کے باوجود شوہر نان و نفقہ ادا نہیں کرتا تو اس عورت کے شوہر سے کہا جائے کہ تم یا تو اپنی بیوی کے حقوق ادا کرو یا طلاق دے دو درینہ تفریق واقع کر دیں گے ۔ اس کے بعد بھی اگر وہ شوہر کسی صورت عمل نہ کرے
هذا الحكو عند المالكية لا يختص بخشية الزنا وافلاس الزوجه لكن لونا خذ منه هيهو على الاطلاق بل أخذناه حيث وجدت الضرورة المسوغ للخروج عن المذهب ١٢ منه
کے جماعت مسلمین و نیز سلان مالم کا مفصل بیان جز ے کے مقدمہ میں گذر چکا ہے اس کا لاحظ ضروری ہے۔
[Heading: Ruling on the recalcitrant husband in maintenance] A husband neglectful of his wife's rights, rebellious. In sharia terminology, 'muta'annit' refers to the person who, despite having the ability, does not fulfill his wife's rights of food and maintenance etc. His ruling too, at times of severe necessity for the relief of oppressed women, has been taken from the Maliki school. Question: If a person, despite having the means, does not fulfill his wife's rights of clothing and maintenance, does his wife have the right to separate herself from his marriage in any way? If so, what is its form? (2) If the qadi can effect separation between them, then when the qadi has pronounced divorce on the wife of that recalcitrant person who does not give maintenance, at that time or after that, if the recalcitrant reform from his ways and promises to fulfill maintenance and other rights, will that woman return to that person? And if she can return to him, is there any difference before the 'iddah and after the 'iddah, or before a second marriage and after a second marriage? Answer: (1) For the wife of a recalcitrant, it is first necessary that she somehow seek a remedy from her husband etc., but if despite extraordinary efforts no solution is possible, then in a state of extreme necessity, it is permissible to act according to the Maliki school, for according to them the wife of a recalcitrant can obtain the right of separation. And there are two types of extreme necessity: First, that no arrangement for the woman's expenses can be made, i.e., neither does any person arrange for her expenses of food and maintenance, nor does she herself have the ability to earn income while preserving her modesty and honor. And the second type of necessity is that although with difficulty or hardship an arrangement for food and maintenance can be made, but there is a strong fear of falling into sin by living separately from the husband. And the form of separation is that the woman should present her case to a qadi (sharia judge) or a Muslim [authority], and in the absence of both, to a sharia committee/jama'at of Muslims. And the person before whom it is presented should conduct a full investigation through sharia evidence etc. And if the woman's claim is proven true that despite his means the husband does not give food and maintenance, then the husband shall be told: either fulfill your wife's rights or divorce her, otherwise we will effect separation. If after that the husband still does not comply in any way... This ruling according to the Malikis is not restricted to fear of zina or the wife's bankruptcy, but we have taken it where necessity justifying departure from the [Hanafi] school is found. From him. The detailed explanation of the jama'at of Muslims and also [؟] has already passed in the introduction of the part; its observation is necessary.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a legal case (hila) addressing the situation of a husband who is 'muta'annit' — i.e., capable but unwilling to provide maintenance (nafaqah) to his wife. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, begins by defining the term and then frames a question: can such a wife separate herself from the marriage? The answer is that she must first exhaust all efforts to reform the husband. If that fails, and there is 'extreme necessity' (sakht majburi), she may follow the Maliki school, which allows a wife to obtain judicial separation (tafriq) due to non-maintenance. Two types of extreme necessity are detailed: (1) absolute inability to arrange for her expenses, and (2) ability to arrange but with strong risk of falling into sin (e.g., temptation due to living apart). The procedure requires taking the case to a qadi or Muslim authority, who investigates and gives the husband an ultimatum: fulfill rights or divorce, else they will separate. The Arabic note at the end clarifies that the Maliki ruling is taken not in its unrestricted form, but only where necessity justifies departing from the Hanafi school. This is a classic example of 'taking from another madhhab' in dire circumstances, a principle of rasm al-mufti.

Key Terms
متعنت (muta'annit): A husband who has the means but refuses to provide maintenance and other rights to his wife.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Food, clothing, and shelter that a husband is obliged to provide for his wife.
تفریق (tafriq): Judicial separation or annulment of marriage by a qadi or authority.
قاضی (qadi): A sharia judge who has authority to adjudicate marital disputes and effect separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under which condition may a wife of a recalcitrant husband act upon the Maliki school to seek separation?
A) Whenever the husband fails to pay maintenance for one month.
B) Only after exhausting all efforts and in a state of extreme necessity, where she cannot arrange expenses or faces strong risk of sin.
C) Only if the husband is also abusive.
D) At any time, because non-payment automatically nullifies the marriage.

Key Takeaway
The wife of a muta'annit can obtain separation by adopting the Maliki school only when extreme necessity of the two specified types is established, following a strict procedure.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate
8 min
Applying Maliki Tafriq as a Hila under Extreme Necessity
Explains Maliki tafriq as a hila under necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions of extreme necessity that justify a Hanafi mufti applying the Maliki ruling on judicial separation due to non-maintenance, and construct the procedure for effecting tafriq.

Core Idea
In extreme necessity, a Hanafi mufti may adopt Maliki position to grant tafriq from a stubborn non-maintaining husband.

The Hanafi school ordinarily does not allow judicial separation for non-maintenance of a present husband. However, when necessity reaches extreme levels, a Hanafi mufti may apply the Maliki ruling as a legal stratagem (hila). This lesson parses the conditions, procedure, and post-separation effects of this Maliki-based tafriq, as detailed in Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilat al-Najiyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default Hanafi position and the Maliki alternative
Recall that Hanafi fiqh does not permit tafriq for non-maintenance of a mut'annit (present, capable husband). The Maliki school does permit it. This lesson presents a hila to adopt the Maliki ruling under necessity.
This is not a routine fatwa; it is a necessary departure.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios of severe hardship (darura)
The passage defines two forms: (1) the wife has no means of support whatsoever, (2) even if support is possible with difficulty, she fears falling into sin by living apart. Both justify applying the Maliki ruling.
These are the threshold conditions for the hila.
3
Trace the procedural steps for tafriq
The wife presents her case to a qadi or Muslim committee. Investigation follows. If proven, the husband is warned: pay or divorce, else tafriq. Upon continued refusal, the judge effects a divorce immediately, without waiting period.
This procedure follows the Maliki school's agreed-upon view.
4
Analyze post-tafriq effects
If the husband returns after the iddah, he has no right to take back his wife; a new marriage is needed. If he returns before iddah, the Maliki school has no clear ruling, leading to two possibilities among later muftis.
Contrast with the absent husband case: his recalcitrance is not established in court.
5
Recognize the principle: necessity limits the hila
The Maliki ruling is not taken absolutely; it is only applied where necessity justifies departure from the Hanafi school. This hila is a valid exit, not a general preference.
Common misunderstanding: applying it without extreme hardship is incorrect.

Source Text

ایک یہ کہ عورت کے خرچ کا کوئی انتظام نہ ہو سکے یعنی نہ کوئی شخص صورت کے خرچ نان و نفقہ کا انتظام کرتا ہونہ خود خورت عصمت و عزت کی حفاظت کرتے ہوئے آمدنی پر قدرت رکھتی ہو ۔
اور دوسری صورت مجبوری کی یہ ہے کہ اگرچہ بہولت یا دشواری سے خرچہ نان و نفقہ کا انتظام ہو سکتا ہے لیکن شوہر سے الگ رہنے میں گناہ ہیں مبتلا ہونے کا قوی اندیشہ ہو۔ اور تفریق کی صورت یہ ہے کہ عورت اپنا مقدمہ قاضی شرع یا مسلمان ، اور ان دونوں کے نہ ہونے کی صورت میں (شرعی کمیٹی جماعت مسلمین میں پیش کرے اور جس شخص کے پاس پیش ہو وہ معاملہ کی شرعی شہادت وغیرہ کے ذریعہ سے مکمل تحقیق کرے اور اگر عورت کا دعویٰ صحیح ثابت ہو کہ وسعت کے باوجود شوہر نان و نفقہ ادا نہیں کرتا تو اس عورت کے شوہر سے کہا جائے کہ تم یا تو اپنی بیوی کے حقوق ادا کرو یا طلاق دے دو درینہ تفریق واقع کر دیں گے ۔ اس کے بعد بھی اگر وہ شوہر کسی صورت عمل نہ کرے
له وهذا الحكو عند المالكية لا يختص بخشية الزنا وافلاس الزوجه لكن لونا خذ منه هيهو على الاطلاق بل أخذناه حيث وجدت الضرورة المسوغ للخروج عن المذهب ١٢ منه

تو قاضی یا شرعاً جو شخص اس کے قائم مقام ہو طلاق واقع کرے اس میں کسی مدت کے انتظار اور جہالت کی حضرات مالکیہ کے متفقہ مذہب کے مطابق ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ روایت ۲۳ علامہ صدیق کی روایت سے ظاہر ہے ۔
بیوی کے حقوق سے لا پرواہ ، فیصلہ شرعی کے بعد ٹھیک ہو جاتے ار متعنت شخص اگر اپنی حرکت سے اس وقت بار آئے جبکہ حاکم شرعی) اس کی بیوی پر طلاق واقع کر چکے اور عدت بھی گزر جائے تو اب اُس شخص کا اپنی بیوی پر کسی قسم کا کوئی اختیار باقی نہیں رہتا کیونکہ عدت گزرنے کے بعد رجوع کا حق نہیں رہتا اگر چہ طلاق رجعی ہی ہو البتہ دونوں فریق کی رضا مندی سے نکاح ہو سکتا ہے اور اگر عدت گزرنے سے پہلے پہلے اپنی حرکت سے وہ شوہر باز آجائے اور نفقہ دینے پر آمادہ ہو جائے تو اس سلسلہ میں حضرات مالکیہ کے مذہب میں واضح روایت نہیں۔ اس وجہ سے حضرات مفتیان کرام کے نزدیک دو احتمال ہیں ۔
کے خان قبل ان المتعنت اذارجع عن التعنت بعد العدة فالمرأة لا ترجع إليه بحال كما هو مذكور في هذا المقام والغائب المطلق عليه اذا قدم بعد العدة واثبت خلاف ما اومته فالمرأة لله وان ماند بعد ما ارسل اليه الحاكم كا سیاتی نما الفرق بين تنت الحاضر و مناء النائب حيث لاحق بعد العدة للمتعنت بحال بخلاف الغائب المعاند يجاب بان تفت الحاضر يثبت في مجلس القاضي فتكون له قوة كما اين هو من المختصر مع شرحه حيث قال (روان او مجب) الملاحي عليه باقرار و لا انکار (جس و ادب) بالضرب (شه) أن استمر على عدم الجوب) (حكم عليه بالحق لانه في قوة الاقرار بالحق اه ( صفحه ۳۹۳ جلد ۲ بخلاف عناد الغائب فافه و ١٣ منه -
There is scope to act upon the Maliki school in a state of severe hardship. According to [them], the wife of a recalcitrant husband can obtain separation. There are two forms of severe hardship: one, that no arrangement can be made for the woman's expenses, i.e., neither does any person arrange for her food and maintenance, nor does she herself have the ability to earn while maintaining her modesty and honor. The second form of hardship is that although with difficulty or hardship arrangement of food and maintenance can be made, there is a strong fear of falling into sin by staying separately from the husband. The form of separation is that the woman presents her case to a Sharia judge or to Muslims, and in the absence of both, to a Sharia committee or congregation of Muslims. The person before whom it is presented thoroughly investigates the matter through Sharia testimony etc. If the woman's claim is proven true that the husband does not pay maintenance despite having capacity, then the husband is told: 'Either fulfill your wife's rights or give a divorce, otherwise we will effect separation.' If even then the husband does not act in any way... 'He said: This ruling according to the Malikis is not specific to fear of adultery and the wife's insolvency, but we do not take it absolutely; rather we take it where necessity justifying departure from the [Hanafi] school exists.' ... Then the judge or his deputy effects the divorce; there is no need for waiting period or ignorance according to the agreed-upon Maliki school, as is apparent from the narration of Allama Siddiq. If the recalcitrant person returns from his recalcitrance after the judge has already effected the divorce and the waiting period has passed, then that person has no authority over his wife, because after the passing of the waiting period, the right to take back does not remain, even if it was a revocable divorce. However, with the consent of both parties, a new marriage can take place. And if before the passing of the waiting period the husband returns from his recalcitrance and becomes willing to pay maintenance, then in this matter there is no clear narration in the Maliki school. Hence according to the honorable muftis, there are two possibilities. ... before that, when the recalcitrant returns from recalcitrance after the waiting period, the woman does not return to him at all, as is mentioned in this context. And the absent one who is ordered to pay, when he arrives after the waiting period and proves contrary to what was attributed to him, the woman remains as is. And if he delays after the judge had sent to him, the difference between the present recalcitrant and the absent recalcitrant is that after the waiting period, the present recalcitrant has no right at all, contrary to the absent recalcitrant. It is answered that the present one's recalcitrance is established in the judge's court, so it has force, as is stated in al-Mukhtasar with its commentary: 'If he is ordered to pay, and he refuses, and the judge disciplines him with beating, if he persists in non-compliance, he is judged against for the right because it is like an admission of the right.' (p. 393 vol. 2) contrary to the recalcitrance of the absent one, for that...
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage discusses a legal stratagem (hila) for a Hanafi mufti: in extreme necessity, the mufti may apply the Maliki school's ruling to grant a wife judicial separation (tafriq) due to her husband's failure to provide maintenance (nafaqa) while he is present and capable (mut'annit). The author describes two scenarios of necessity: (1) the wife has no means of support whatsoever, and (2) even if support is possible with difficulty, she fears falling into sin by living apart. The procedure requires the wife to present her case to a Sharia judge or Muslim committee, who investigates thoroughly. If the husband refuses to either pay or divorce despite having the means, the judge warns him and then effects a divorce immediately, without waiting period, following the Maliki position. The passage then addresses the effect of the husband's return: if he returns after the 'iddah, he has no right to take her back; if before the 'iddah, the Maliki school has no clear ruling, leading to two possibilities among later muftis. The text contrasts the present recalcitrant (his defiance is established in court) with the absent one who is ordered to pay but may contest upon return, citing al-Mukhtasar. This hila is permissible only under genuine necessity as a valid exit from the dominant Hanafi position.

Key Terms
متعنت (mut'annit): A husband who is present and able to provide maintenance but stubbornly refuses to do so.
تفریق (tafriq): Judicial separation or divorce pronounced by a qadi or his deputy due to the husband's failure to fulfill marital obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for applying the Maliki tafriq hila?
A) The husband is absent and not paying maintenance.
B) The wife has no means of support and no one to provide for her.
C) The husband has a valid excuse for not paying.
D) The wife has a job and can support herself.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti may apply the Maliki ruling on tafriq only under verified extreme necessity, following a strict procedure of investigation, warning, and immediate divorce upon continued refusal.

Maliki Ruling on Reforming Mutaanit Husband After Judicial Divorce
Explains the Maliki ruling on a husband who reforms after the judge has already divorced his wife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Maliki judicial divorce ruling for a mutaanit husband as a valid hila in Hanafi fatwa practice, and distinguish between the two Maliki opinions on the effect of the husband's recantation within the iddah period.

Core Idea
After judicial divorce, a husband who reforms after iddah loses all rights; within iddah, the preferred view makes the divorce irrevocable.

In Hanafi fiqh, a wife married to a husband who persistently refuses maintenance cannot obtain a judicial divorce. However, scholars of the later period, facing severe hardship, have adopted the Maliki school's ruling as a legal stratagem (hila) to relieve the oppressed wife. This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilat un-Najijah explains the Maliki position on what happens if the stubborn husband reforms after the judge has already divorced his wife. Understanding this ruling allows a Hanafi mufti to navigate cross-madhhab fatwa under necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi gap
Recognize that in the Hanafi school, a wife cannot obtain a judicial divorce solely due to the husband's failure to pay nafaqah. This creates a predicament when the husband is mutaanit (stubbornly neglectful). The solution is to adopt a ruling from another school.
This step frames the necessity for the hila.
2
Examine the Maliki judicial divorce
The Maliki school allows the judge to dissolve the marriage if the husband is unable or unwilling to provide maintenance. The divorce takes effect immediately upon the judge's ruling, with no waiting period required.
This is the core of the hila.
3
Analyze the two Maliki opinions on recantation
The text presents two probabilities if the husband recants within the iddah: one treats the divorce as revocable (raj'i), the other as irrevocable (bain). The preferred opinion, endorsed by Allamah Salih and the author, is that it is irrevocable.
The distinction has practical consequences: under the revocable view, the husband can take her back without consent; under the irrevocable view, a new marriage is required.
4
Apply the hila in fatwa
As a Hanafi mufti, you may issue a fatwa based on this Maliki ruling under necessity. The adopted position is that even if the husband reforms within iddah, the divorce is irrevocable; she must return only if he recants (since revocation does not need her consent), but it is better to renew the marriage contract as a precaution.
This step ties the source to practical iftaa.

تو قاضی یا شرعاً جو شخص اس کے قائم مقام ہو طلاق واقع کرے اس میں کسی مدت کے انتظار اور جہالت کی حضرات مالکیہ کے متفقہ مذہب کے مطابق ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ روایت ۲۳ علامہ صدیق کی روایت سے ظاہر ہے ۔
بیوی کے حقوق سے لا پرواہ ، فیصلہ شرعی کے بعد ٹھیک ہو جاتے ار متعنت شخص اگر اپنی حرکت سے اس وقت بار آئے جبکہ حاکم شرعی) اس کی بیوی پر طلاق واقع کر چکے اور عدت بھی گزر جائے تو اب اُس شخص کا اپنی بیوی پر کسی قسم کا کوئی اختیار باقی نہیں رہتا کیونکہ عدت گزرنے کے بعد رجوع کا حق نہیں رہتا اگر چہ طلاق رجعی ہی ہو البتہ دونوں فریق کی رضا مندی سے نکاح ہو سکتا ہے اور اگر عدت گزرنے سے پہلے پہلے اپنی حرکت سے وہ شوہر باز آجائے اور نفقہ دینے پر آمادہ ہو جائے تو اس سلسلہ میں حضرات مالکیہ کے مذہب میں واضح روایت نہیں۔ اس وجہ سے حضرات مفتیان کرام کے نزدیک دو احتمال ہیں ۔
كے [؟] قبل ان المتعنت اذارجع عن التعنت بعد العدة فالمرأة لا ترجع إليه بحال كما هو مذكور في هذا المقام والغائب المطلق عليه اذا قدم بعد العدة واثبت خلاف ما اومته فالمرأة لله وان ماند بعد ما ارسل اليه الحاكم كا سیاتی نما الفرق بين تنت الحاضر و مناء النائب حيث لاحق بعد العدة للمتعنت بحال بخلاف الغائب المعاند يجاب بان تفت الحاضر يثبت في مجلس القاضي فتكون له قوة كما اين هو من المختصر مع شرحه حيث قال (روان او مجب) الملاحي عليه باقرار و لا انکار (جس و ادب) بالضرب (شه) أن استمر على عدم الجوب) (حكم عليه بالحق لانه في قوة الاقرار بالحق اه ( صفحه ۳۹۳ جلد ۲ بخلاف عناد الغائب فافه و ١٣ منه -
So the judge or whoever is his substitute in Shariah should effect the divorce; there is no need for waiting for a period or ignorance according to the unanimous Maliki school. As is evident from tradition 23 from Sayyid Siddiq. Neglect of the wife's rights are rectified after the Shariah ruling. And if the stubborn person recants from his behavior at a time when the Shariah ruler has already effected divorce on his wife and the iddah has passed, then that person retains no authority over his wife whatsoever, because after the iddah the right of return does not remain, even if the divorce was revocable. However, with mutual consent a new marriage can take place. And if the recants before the iddah has passed and becomes ready to pay maintenance, then there is no clear narration in the Maliki school regarding this matter. For this reason, the honored muftis have two probabilities: one is that this separation be considered a revocable divorce and revocation be held valid within the iddah. The other probability is that this separation be considered an irrevocable divorce and the husband not be given the authority to return the wife to marriage. But Allamah Salih held that the first probability (i.e., making it irrevocable) is more correct and better. As is found in the tradition and in the summary of Allamah Salih's fatwa. We also find his opinion and fatwa correct after considering the excuse. For this reason, our fatwa is that if the husband recants from his stubbornness (neglect of rights) within the iddah, the woman must remain with him, whether she is pleased or not, because the wife's consent is not necessary for revocation. However, it is better to perform a new marriage if there is precaution.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Maliki school on the situation of a husband (mutaanit) who neglects his wife's maintenance, leading to judicial divorce. The text discusses the consequences if the husband reforms. After the judge has pronounced divorce, if the iddah has already expired, the husband has no right to take her back; a new nikah with her consent is possible. If he reforms before the iddah ends, the Maliki school has two opinions: some treat the divorce as revocable, allowing the husband to return without a new marriage; others treat it as irrevocable (bain). The preferred view, endorsed by Allamah Salih and followed by the author, is that the divorce is irrevocable even if he reforms within the iddah—the wife must stay with him if he recants, because revocation does not require her consent, but it is recommended to renew the marriage contract as a precaution. The passage then notes a distinction between a present stubborn husband and an absent one, citing a Maliki text to show that the present one's stubbornness is considered an implicit admission of wrongdoing, strengthening the judge's decision. The lesson is a classic example of a hila (legal stratagem) from the Maliki school to resolve a situation where the Hanafi school does not grant the wife a right to judicial divorce for non-maintenance. The mufti here adopts this Maliki ruling as a fatwa for severe necessity, in order to relieve the oppressed woman.

Key Terms
متعنت (mutaanit): A husband who persistently refuses to fulfill his marital obligations, especially maintenance, without legitimate excuse.
طلاق رجعی (talaq raj'i): A revocable divorce during the iddah period where the husband can return without a new marriage.
طلاق بائن (talaq bain): An irrevocable divorce after which reunion requires a new marriage and the wife's consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Maliki ruling presented in this passage, what happens if the husband reforms after the iddah has passed?
A) He may take his wife back without a new marriage.
B) He has no authority over her, but they can remarry with mutual consent.
C) The wife must return to him whether she agrees or not.
D) The divorce is automatically annulled.

Key Takeaway
The Maliki judicial divorce for a mutaanit husband serves as a hila for Hanafis, and the preferred opinion treats the divorce as irrevocable, requiring a new marriage for reunion.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate
7 min
Hila for Wife of Absent Husband Using Maliki Fiqh
Legal stratagem for wife of absent husband using Maliki fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the hila for a wife of an absent non-missing husband and identify the steps required to obtain tafriq under Maliki fiqh.

Core Idea
When a husband is absent and fails to provide, the wife may use Maliki fiqh to obtain judicial separation via qadi.

This passage presents a legal stratagem (hila) for a wife whose husband is absent but traceable and neglects maintenance. While the Hanafi school does not easily grant judicial separation for lack of maintenance, it permits adopting the Maliki ruling in cases of severe necessity. The stratagem involves proving the marriage and non-maintenance before a qadi to obtain tafriq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
The husband is absent (ghaib ghair mafqud), known location, but does not provide maintenance, visit, or divorce. The wife is distressed.
This is not a mafqud (missing) case; different rules would apply.
2
Attempt Khul' First
The first recommended step is to persuade the husband to agree to khul' (divorce by compensation). If he agrees, the matter is resolved.
Khul' requires husband's consent in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Resort to Maliki Hila if Necessary
If khul' fails and the wife cannot bear the hardship patiently, and severe necessity (darurah) exists, she may adopt the Maliki method.
The Maliki school allows tafriq for non-maintenance even without the husband's consent.
4
Follow the Judicial Procedure
The wife must present her case to a qadi (judge), prove the marriage through witnesses, then prove that the husband fails to provide food and maintenance. The qadi then issues a decree of tafriq (judicial separation).
After tafriq, the wife is free to remarry. If the husband returns later, he does not automatically regain marital rights.
5
Handle the Husband's Return
If the husband returns after tafriq, the wife does not revert to him automatically. He may need to remarry if both wish to reunite, subject to conditions.
This prevents the husband from abandoning maintenance and reclaiming the wife at will.

غائب غیر مفقود کی بیوی کا حکم اور یہ بھی فقہ مالک سے ماخوذ ہے تاکہ اس کو نجات حاصل ہو سکے۔ بوقت ضرورت شدیده مظلومه عورت کو یہ صورت اختیار کرنی چاہیے۔ سوال: جو شخص نائب ہو جائے اور اس کا پتہ معلوم ہے لیکن نہ تو وہ خود آتا ہے اور نہ بیوی کو اپنے پاس بلاتا ہے نہ اس کے خرچ وغیرہ کا کوئی انتظام کرتا ہے اور نہ طلاق دیتا، اس وجہ سے عورت تنگ اور پریشان ہے تو کیا اس کی بیوی کے لیے کوئی راستہ ہے کہ اُس غائب کے نکاح سے خود کو علیحدہ کرے؟ اور دوسری جگہ نکاح کرے۔ (۲) تفریق کی صورت میں اگر تفریق کے بعد دوسرے شوہر سے پہلے یا دوسرا نکاح کرنے کے بعد وہ شخص واپس آجائے اور نان و نفقہ کا انتظام کرنے پر آمادہ ہو تو کیا بیوی اس کو مل جائے گی، اور اگر واپس مل جاتی ہے تو کن شرائط اور کیس تفضیل کے ساتھ واپس ملتی ہے ؟ الجواب : غائب غیر مفقود کی بیوی کیلئے ایک سہولت حضرات اللہ کے متفقہ فیصلہ کے ساتھ اس عورت کی رہائی کے لیے جو صورت صحیح ہے وہ تو یہ ہے کہ اس کے شوہر کو ضلع پر رضامند کیا جائے اگر شوہر خلع پر بھی رضامند نہ ہو تو پھر اگر یہ عورت مبر کے ساتھ با صمت زندگی گزار سکے تو بہتر ہے ورنہ جب نان و نفقہ اور گذر اوقات کے لیے کوئی صورت ممکن نہ ہو تو سخت مجبور نہیں یہ بھی گنجانش ہے کہ مذہب مالکیہ کے موافق مندرجہ ذیل صورت اختیار کر کے رہائی حاصل کرے۔ وہ صورت یہ ہے کہ عورت قاضی کے پاس مقدمہ پیش کر کے گواہان سے اُس نائب شخص کے ساتھ اپنا نکاح ہونا ثابت کرے پھر یہ ثابت کرے کہ وہ شخص نان و نفقہ نہیں دیتا، پھر قاضی اس کے حق میں تفریق کا فیصلہ صادر کرے۔
The ruling of the wife of an absent non-missing husband, and this is also derived from Maliki fiqh so that she may obtain relief. At times of severe necessity, the oppressed woman should adopt this method. Question: A person who becomes absent and his whereabouts are known, but he neither comes himself nor calls his wife to him, nor makes any arrangement for her expenses etc., nor divorces her; because of this the woman is distressed and worried. Is there any way for his wife to separate herself from that absent man's marriage and marry elsewhere? (2) In the case of tafriq, if after tafriq before another husband or after marrying another, that person returns and is willing to arrange for food and maintenance, will the wife be returned to him? And if she is returned, under what conditions and with what preference is she returned? Answer: For the wife of an absent non-missing husband, with the unanimous decision of the scholars of Allah, the correct method for this woman's release is that her husband be persuaded to agree to khul'. If the husband is not willing even to khul', then if this woman can live patiently with [؟], it is better. Otherwise, when no way for food, maintenance, and livelihood is possible, then in severe necessity, this also is permissible that she adopt the following method according to the Maliki school and obtain release. That method is that the woman present a case before the qadi, prove her marriage with that absent man through witnesses, then prove that he does not provide food and maintenance, then the qadi passes a judgment of tafriq in her favor.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage presents a hila (legal stratagem) drawn from the Maliki madhhab to help a wife whose husband is absent but not missing (ghaib ghair mafqud) and fails to provide maintenance. The author outlines a step-by-step solution: the wife should first attempt to secure khul' (divorce by compensation) from the husband. If that fails and she cannot endure the hardship, she may resort to Maliki fiqh by taking her case to a qadi. She must prove her marriage and the husband's failure to provide maintenance. The qadi then issues a decree of judicial separation (tafriq). This is a classic example of talfiq (piecing together rulings from different schools) to alleviate hardship, a principle accepted in the Hanafi school for fatwa when necessity arises.

Key Terms
غائب غیر مفقود (ghaib ghair mafqud): A husband who is absent but whose whereabouts are known; not missing.
خلع (khul‘): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation to the husband.
تفریق (tafriq): Judicial separation ordered by a qadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under the hila described, who is responsible for granting the tafriq?
A) The husband's family
B) A Hanafi mufti
C) A qadi (judge)
D) The wife herself

Key Takeaway
The hila for wife of absent husband shows how Hanafi fatwa borrows Maliki tafriq in severe necessity, emphasizing judicial process and evidence.
